Current Events Commentary

The Wrong Path of American Policy Towards China

— Hoshino

Since the economic and financial panic in our country began, our diplomacy towards Japan has taken a sharp turn. All the powers with interests in the Far East are in a state of panic, devising countermeasures. Among these countries, the one most troubled and hesitant, in our estimation, is probably the United States. According to a Washington dispatch, U.S. Under Secretary of State Philipps has consulted with the British Ambassador to the United States, Lindsay, on the China issue. They plan to reorganize the international banking consortium based on the Nine-Power Treaty to help China overcome its current economic and financial difficulties and avoid the desperation of choosing anything to eat in times of famine. We are now in a dilemma, facing both a fierce tiger in front and a deep abyss behind. We need not harbor extravagant hopes, nor need we favor one over the other. However, at this point, we cannot help but regret the lack of a definite Far East policy in the United States, focusing only on the present and not considering the long term.

Everyone knows that America's policy towards China in the Far East is one of open door and territorial integrity. However, this is not a policy, but merely a slogan. To implement a country's policy, it should be revised according to local conditions and the times. However, the fundamental spirit must be pursued with all efforts. Japan's pursuit of its continental policy and Britain's pursuit of its Suez policy are both examples of this. However, the U.S. government, clinging to its traditional isolationism and the Monroe Doctrine, and relying on its geographical and national strength, often starts strong but ends weakly when it comes to foreign policy, or promises benefits but does not deliver. Its promotion of the League of Nations, its advocacy of the London Economic Conference, its proposal to not recognize puppet states, and its interpretation of the "over-negotiation" point in the Treaty of Paris all contradict theory and practice, and its claims are divorced from action. This makes countries around the world often doubt whether the United States can "see things through from beginning to end."

China's survival in East Asia depends solely on self-reliance and striving. However, for China's allies, if they have no territorial or political ambitions, they should recognize that a strong and prosperous China is the best guarantee of the interests of the powers. In other words, how to enable China to achieve genuine unity and positive construction as soon as possible, and improve the living standards and purchasing power of the Chinese people, so as to achieve the goal of benefiting others and oneself. However, countries often lack foresight. Although there are provisions in the Nine-Power Treaty guaranteeing China's opportunity for self-development, they are willing to sacrifice future gains for immediate interests, just like the saying goes, "killing the goose that lays the golden eggs." Japan's occupation of our four northeastern provinces goes without saying. Even Soviet Russia is now eyeing Xinjiang. France is reluctant to concede in the Sino-French Vietnam Treaty. All are doing the same. What disappoints us the most is that the United States, which China has always regarded as a good friend, is also stubbornly pursuing its silver policy, making China's economic difficulties increasingly acute. Its lack of enthusiasm for maintaining the "open door" policy and its lack of effort in cooperating with the powers make us doubt whether the American diplomatic authorities have a consistent position and basic attitude.

Now, the Far East issue is not far from a comprehensive resolution. The American people should have the determination to either move forward or retreat, and there is no possibility of wandering down a wrong path. The policy of isolationism is difficult to sustain in today's economically interdependent world. Those who are clear about the world situation all know this. Cooperation among the powers in the Far East is relatively feasible and more in line with the direction of peace. However, cooperation among the powers often follows the lead of the United States. This is because the United States is the initiator of the Nine-Power Treaty, its national strength is stronger than that of Britain, France, and Russia, and its future hopes in the Far East are greater than those of European countries. If the American authorities can truly recognize the mistakes of wandering down a wrong path and the shortsightedness of seeking temporary security, then they should determine their direction and clarify their attitude as soon as possible. For the Far East issue, the first step is to change their silver policy to avoid China's economic and financial difficulties. The second step is to actively lead the major powers under the principles of the Nine-Power Treaty to provide a practical solution to the Far East issue. This is not only what world peace depends on, but also where American interests lie. May the wise American government authorities consider this carefully.

International Loans to China Under Careful Study by the U.S.; Suggestion to the U.K. to Postpone Reply

(Washington) President Roosevelt recently announced that the U.S. government is currently studying the possibility of providing financial assistance to China internationally. The U.K. recently inquired about the U.S.'s opinion on this matter, but the U.S. is not yet prepared to respond. (Havas dispatch on the 6th)

(Tokyo) As of now, the U.K. and the U.S. have only exchanged opinions regarding assistance to China and have not yet touched upon specific strategies. The Japanese government has no objection to separately discussing the China issue with countries with common interests. (Dentsu dispatch on the 7th)

Japanese Commercial Attaché Yokotake Discusses Sino-Japanese Cooperation; Improving Agricultural Technology Stationed in China

Osaka The Osaka Chamber of Commerce and Industry invited Commercial Attaché Yokotake stationed in Shanghai on the 6th to discuss the issue of Sino-Japanese cooperation. Mr. Yokotake stated at the meeting, "Although the Chinese government has explicitly stated that it prohibits anti-Japanese movements, we must temporarily observe the situation. China is an agricultural country, but due to natural disasters and other reasons, it imports 200 million yuan worth of rice, wheat, cotton, sugar, etc. every year. If Japan assists in improving its agricultural technology and agricultural products, making China a powerful raw material producing country, and cooperates with Japan's industrial technology, then the substance of Sino-Japanese cooperation can be realized." (Nichiren dispatch on the 8th)

New Japanese Military Attaché to China of Significant Nature; Major General Isoya Known as a China Expert; A Powerful Figure of the Younger Generation

(Tokyo) The regular transfer of army personnel was approved by the Emperor on the 5th at the request of Minister of the Army Hayashi. The details were announced on the evening of the 6th and will be officially ordered on the 12th or 13th. The main personnel changes are as follows:

Military Attaché to the Chinese Embassy Suzuki Mitsu, transferred to Commander of the 19th Division in Ranam, Korea; Chief of the Second Department of the General Staff Isoya Ren, transferred to Military Attaché to the Chinese Embassy; Chief of the Army Transportation Department Miyake Mitsuharu, transferred to Commander of the 20th Division (Ryuzan, Korea); Commander of the Shimonoseki Fortress Shimomoto Kumaya, transferred to Commander of the 0th Division; 00 Commander Hayashi Zo Kiyoshi, transferred to Commander of the Shimonoseki Fortress; Okamura Yasuji of the General Staff Headquarters, transferred to Chief of the Second Department; Suzuki Shigeyasu transferred to Chief of the First Department.

Major General Isoya, in the Second Department of the General Staff, is well-versed in all aspects of the situation and is also familiar with China's affairs within the army. His appointment as Military Attaché to China is of great significance. (Nichiren dispatch on the 6th)

Taiwanese Capitalists to Japan to Meet Li Zeyi; To Propose Joint Development of Fujian Province

(Tokyo) Taiwanese capitalist Gu Xianrong, hearing that Li Zeyi had arrived in Kyoto, has come to Kyoto from Taiwan and plans to meet with Li Zeyi. Gu will propose to Li cooperation in the industrial construction of Fujian and issues related to the railway and mining in southern Fujian. (Hualian dispatch on the 7th)

New King of Siam Ascends the Throne at a Young Age; State Affairs Handled by the Regency Council; Similar to the King of Yugoslavia; Attempted Assassination of the Minister of Defense Fails

Bangkok Prince Ananda Mahidol, nephew of the former King of Siam, who is eleven years old, ascended the throne as King of Siam today. Before he comes of age, all state affairs will be handled by the Regency Council. The King of Siam's parents are currently residing in Lausanne, Switzerland, and will come here soon. The former King of Siam is now residing in England and has changed his name to Prince Sukhothai. (Reuters dispatch on the 7th)

Bangkok Today, the proclamation was made that the eleven-year-old prince, nephew of the king, is the new monarch of Siam. This is the second young ruler in recent months to ascend the throne at the same age. The new king, Prince Ananda, is the nephew of the King of Siam, who abdicated last week and retired with his Queen to Surrey, England. The Siamese government has organized a Regency Council to assist the young ruler until he comes of age. The chairman of the Regency Council is Prince Anuwatna. The new King of Siam, Ananda Mahidol, and King Peter II of Yugoslavia both ascended the throne at a young age. Although both countries are ruled by a regency, the people of both countries await the coronation of the new king and the future of the royal family. The experience of Peter II was far more tragic than that of the new King of Siam, because his father, King Alexander, was assassinated while visiting Versailles. The accession of the new King Ananda this time was due to the King of Siam's voluntary abdication because the cabinet rejected his proposed reforms. However, the official statement released today stated that the King abdicated on March 2. This morning, there was an attempt to assassinate Minister of Defense Siri Ratnuthu, which was thwarted. The edict of the new king's succession to the throne has stabilized the tense atmosphere in the country. Prior to this, the government kept the new king's movements a secret and strictly censored the news to prevent leaks. Some quarters have stated that the people have repeatedly requested the former king to continue on the throne, so the news of the former king's abdication may cause some political turmoil. The army is now in control of all government agencies and will effectively rule the country until the new king is formally proclaimed. It is said that for the sake of protecting the new king, all activities will be prevented to demonstrate to the former king. The King of Siam ascended the throne in 1925 and had absolute power, but the King did not like the vast power. The King wanted to educate his people and instill knowledge in them, at least to enable the people to participate in politics. The King proposed promulgating a constitution. Powerful princes opposed this proposal because their power would be shaken, but the Nationalist Party cooperated with the King and eventually won. Although Siam implemented an autonomous system, the King continued to educate the people tirelessly. Many people thought he was too radical, but the world believed that Siam was in the most stable position in this turbulent world. It is said that the king's return to the throne is still possible, as the young King Michael of Romania recently abdicated to his father, King Carol. The new king is the king's beloved nephew, and some quarters have stated that the king only needs to lift a finger to remove all obstacles. When the king abdicated, he drafted many decrees, the most important of which was that the power to make the final judgment on the death penalty should be in the hands of the king. The king left many other plans for educating the people and defining the powers of parliament. (National Telegram on the 7th)

Amidst Italian-Ethiopian Compromise Rumors, Italian Air Force Opens in East Africa; Governor-General of Italian Somaliland Officially Appointed

Cairo Although Italy and Ethiopia are currently brewing a compromise, Italy still wants to send a large number of planes to its African colonies. The number is still uncertain, but it is estimated to be around 400. It is currently discussing with the Egyptian government the issue of passing through Egyptian territory. (National Telegraph on the 6th)

Rome General Graziani, Commander-in-Chief of the Italian East African Expeditionary Force, has now been appointed Governor-General of Italian Somaliland. In addition, one thousand aviation personnel and aircraft were loaded onto ships in Genoa tonight and transported to East Africa. Italian aircraft factories are currently speeding up construction to replenish the aviation materials transported to East Africa. (Havas Dispatch on the 7th)

Messina, Italy The steamship "Ganges" carrying a regiment of infantry, two artillery companies, a number of engineering teams, and military supplies, set sail from here and headed for East Africa. (Havas dispatch on the 6th)

France Strengthens its Military; Naval Construction Program Submitted to Parliament Yesterday; Cabinet Discusses Extending Military Service Period

(Paris) The government today proposed to the House of Representatives to build a main battleship and two 1,700-ton destroyers by the end of this year, and to begin construction of another battleship after January 1937. The tonnage of the main battleship has not been announced, but according to non-official sources, it is likely to be 35,000 tons. Some quarters say that France's move is a response to the naval turmoil that has been plaguing the world diplomatic community, in which France has been seen as a secondary player, so it is building ships as a response. France's naval status is the fourth in the world, with a total of 500,000 tons, including nine main battleships. Japan also has nine, while the United Kingdom and the United States each have fifteen. The government's request to the House of Representatives today does not exceed France's quota under the Five-Power Treaty. (National Telegraph on the 4th)

(Paris) At a special cabinet meeting today, a decision may be made to increase the military service period from one year to two years. This is because during the war years from 1914 to 1918, the birth rate declined, resulting in a decrease in the annual number of conscripts from 240,000 to 120,000. This will begin this year and will continue until 1939. It is believed that the radical members of the government are advocating delaying the decision until after the municipal elections on May 5, as the public is largely opposed to increasing the military service period. (Reuters dispatch on the 7th)

(Paris) After the cabinet met today to discuss increasing the term of military service, it issued a communiqué in the afternoon stating that no decision had been made on the matter. (Reuters dispatch on the 7th)

Anglo-German Talks Postponed; British Labor Party Members Severely Reprimand; Hitler Claims Illness; Foreign Secretary Blocked; White Paper on Defense Policy a Real Escalation; Impeachment Motion to be Filed Monday; Simon Awaits German Response; Eden Prepares for Trip to Russia and Poland

(London) The Labor Party members in the House of Commons today strongly criticized the government's White Paper on defense issues and questioned Foreign Secretary Simon on the reasons for postponing his trip to Germany. The Labor Party believes that the real reason for the postponement is this White Paper. When Simon mentioned that German Chancellor Hitler was currently suffering from a cold, Labor Party members laughed wildly. Simon replied that the German Foreign Minister had informed the British Ambassador in Berlin yesterday that the German Chancellor had caught a cold and lost his voice when returning to the Saar, so the scheduled talks with British cabinet members this week had to be postponed. The German government was very sorry for this. When asked when the talks would likely take place, Simon replied that he was in contact with the German government on this matter. Then, Labor Party leader Lansbury rose and asked if the Foreign Secretary could advise his colleagues to withdraw the White Paper pending the Anglo-German talks. Simon replied that he could not, and indeed could not. Lansbury continued to ask whether the Foreign Secretary thought that publishing an unfriendly document such as the Defense White Paper would promote friendly negotiations. Simon replied that this matter would be discussed on Monday when the House of Commons debates defense issues. Labor Party member Cox suggested that the Foreign Secretary should go to Moscow first, as the authorities there had not lost their voices, which caused much laughter and ended the discussion. According to today's news, the Labor Party will propose a vote of impeachment against the government when the House of Commons debates defense on Monday and will ask the House to express its opinion on the government's defense policy, that is, whether the government's policy is fully in line with the spirit of establishing a League of Nations to lay the foundation for collective world peace, whether it will greatly hinder any hopes for a disarmament convention, and whether it will lead to international competition and insecurity and ultimately to war. When the cabinet met this afternoon, it discussed the postponement of Simon's trip to Germany. Cabinet members believed that it would eventually take place after Hitler recovered. The Foreign Secretary's preparations for his trip to Moscow and Warsaw have not been suspended due to the postponement of his trip to Berlin, but the government still hopes that Hitler will recover soon so that Simon and Eden can go to Germany first and proceed according to the original plan. (Reuters dispatch on the 6th)

(London) Lord Privy Seal Eden will soon go to Warsaw and Moscow to conduct negotiations with the Soviet and Polish governments on the Anglo-French Declaration of February 3. On Monday, Eden will announce in the House of Commons the various preparations for his trip to Russia and Poland. As for whether German Chancellor Hitler has recovered and when Foreign Secretary Simon can go to Berlin, the response from Germany is currently awaited here. (Havas on the 7th)

(London) The cabinet held a cabinet meeting today to discuss the situation caused by Foreign Secretary Simon's postponement of his trip to Germany. As a result, it was decided that the British government's proposal to send representatives to Moscow and Warsaw should not be hindered by Hitler's illness. If Herr Hitler's health recovers within days and he is prepared to meet with Foreign Secretary Simon and Lord Privy Seal Eden, then Simon and Eden will still travel to Germany first. Regarding this matter, Simon and Berlin are currently in communication. British officials are unwilling to question the reasons given by Hitler for requesting the postponement of the Anglo-German talks (referring to Herr Hitler's illness), but they are quite surprised by the attacks launched by German newspapers against the British government after the publication of the White Paper on defense policy. Some figures regarding Germany's rearmament have been circulating here. It is said that at the end of 1934, Germany's military expenditures and the expenses of military groups other than the regular army increased by more than 1,100,000,000 marks compared to 1933, while the increase listed in the budget was only 605,000,000 marks. The total military budget reached 2,000,000,000 marks, which exceeds the British defense budget. Now Germany is expressing indignation at the British budget, which is completely unreasonable. (Havas dispatch on the 6th)

Japan's Kanagawa and Nara Prefectures Plan to Build Giant Bronze Buddha Statues

(Tokyo) The Nichiren sect has decided to build a large bronze Buddha statue in the Tokai Betsuin on Mount Minobu in Kanagawa Prefecture. The platform will be 40 feet high, the Buddha statue will be 70 feet high, for a total of 110 feet. The face will be 14 feet long, the ears will be 5 feet long, the eyes will be 3 feet 5 inches long, the mouth will be 4 feet 5 inches long, and the circumference of the Buddha's body will be 96 feet. The cost will be 500,000 yuan. Construction will begin this autumn and is scheduled to be completed in three years. (Nichiren News Agency dispatch on the 7th)

The Rebellious Faction Resorts to Defiant Resistance; Greek National Army Begins Offensive; Air Force Heavily Bombs Rebel Positions, Inflicting Severe Damage; Venizelos Sails Towards the Mediterranean by Ship

Athens - Because the rebel faction refused the ultimatum, the government has launched a final and forceful suppression. This morning, government troops, after a fierce bombardment, crossed the Struma River and launched a strong attack on enemy positions. As it is the dead of winter, the rebels are in dire straits and may not be able to hold out for long. The government troops are personally commanded by General Kondylis. Before the government troops launched their offensive, they used aircraft to heavily bomb the area near Kavala on the Macedonian coast, where the rebels were heavily concentrated, inflicting severe damage. When the planes dropped bombs from the sky and strafed the streets with machine guns at low altitude, the 50,000 residents of the town were greatly alarmed. (Reuters, 7th)

Alexandria - News received here this morning stated that two cruisers occupied by Greek rebels are now heading towards this port. Former Prime Minister Venizelos is also said to be on board. This caused great shock among the people. The Egyptian government has today ordered that if the Greek rebel ships seek refuge in the port of Alexandria, the weapons of the crew members should be confiscated, the breechblocks of the cannons removed, and their ammunition confiscated. Police are stationed at all key points in the city to prevent demonstrations by those who sympathize with the Greek revolution and Venizelos's party. Meanwhile, according to a Reuters correspondent in Athens, one of the cruisers belonging to the rebels has arrived off the coast of Dattilo Island in the Aegean Sea today. (Reuters, 7th)

General Offensive Delayed Due to Bad Weather

(Vienna) According to the latest news from Athens, the reason why yesterday's general offensive could not be carried out was due to bad weather. However, it will definitely be held within the next 24 hours. Currently, both sides are doing their best to strengthen their fighting power in preparation for the decisive battle. (National Telegram, 7th)

Salonika, Greece - The Minister of the Army, Kondylis, issued the following public announcement at 8 PM tonight: Although the weather is currently extremely cold, government troops are continuing to advance towards the front lines. The transportation of supplies to the rear has not been obstructed. By noon today, the weather gradually improved. A large squadron of bombers attempted to fly to the enemy's position, but due to cloud cover, they were unable to take action and immediately returned. However, two of the planes bravely broke through the clouds and dropped bombs on the enemy barracks in Serres and the enemy troops in Xigalkebanli from a low altitude of 20 meters above the ground. The rebels in Serres are now in a state of chaos. According to news from Eastern Macedonia Province, the rebels have been routed one after another, and the situation is extremely dire. At the Aliakmon River front line, the rebel forces are weak and cannot stand against the government troops. If the weather is clear tomorrow, the government troops can make a major advance. In short, the only reason for not immediately suppressing the rebellion is the weather. As for suppressing the turmoil, it is no longer a problem. The people of Salonika are now quietly awaiting the development of events and have consistently expressed their trust in the government. The first batch of those who died in the previous conflict with the rebels were buried at 2 PM today. The public all went to the funeral to express their opposition to the rebellion. (Havas, 6th)

The Government is Confident of Victory

Athens - Since the Minister of the Army, Kondylis, personally led his troops to the front lines, the progress of the army has been affected by the bad weather. However, Kondylis declared that he has decided to fight the rebels to the finish in Serres. Last night, there was heavy rain and snow here, and tonight there is a thick layer of fog. The rebel position is only ten miles away from the national army. According to Kondylis, only 2,000 of the rebels have adequate weapons. Even at the time of battle, if the rebels increase their forces to 10,000, the government can mobilize 100,000, so victory is practically assured. The leaders of the national army have sent a telegram to the Prime Minister, stating that the discipline and morale of the national army are perfect, and that the rebels can be annihilated when the weather clears up in the coming days. Within the capital, all traces of rebellion have been eliminated, and about a thousand people with suspicious behavior have been arrested. Military officers who have not gained the full trust of the government have also been replaced. The arsenals are repairing the warships destroyed by the rebels day and night. Today, the government reissued a decree that the property of all rebel personnel and their relatives will be confiscated, all Greek ships are prohibited from entering Greek ports, and foreign ships will also be subject to strict inspection. (National Telegram, 6th)

Roosevelt Expresses No Intention to Further Reduce the Value of Currency; The Time is Not Yet Ripe to Stabilize Prices

(Washington) - President Roosevelt told reporters at the White House this afternoon that the international effort to provide China with loans is under consideration, but in the past half month, he has not heard of any progress in this matter. President Roosevelt continued to talk about prices but declined to comment on the suggestion of continuing to reduce the gold value of the dollar. He said the government hopes to reduce the burden of debt, but he feels that prices have not yet reached a sufficient level to make this burden relatively lighter. Therefore, he believes that the time is not yet ripe to stabilize domestic prices. Several sources in New York believe that President Roosevelt's statement is a veiled reference to the British monetary authorities, meaning that the pound is so low that it may suppress American prices, in which case the United States will take retaliatory action to deal with it. However, Wall Street is quite confused about the true meaning of President Roosevelt's remarks, because last autumn President Roosevelt also made similar remarks about raising prices. (Reuters, 6th)

(Washington) - President Roosevelt spoke with reporters this morning, and speculators may have misunderstood the President's meaning. This afternoon, White House aides claimed that the President had no intention of further reducing the value of the dollar, and there was absolutely no hint in the President's statement that could be interpreted as implying a reduction in the value of the dollar. When the President spoke with reporters, he said that he believed the purchasing power of the dollar could still be adjusted to reduce people's debts. Although the debt burden has been reduced a lot, it is still far from enough. At that time, someone asked if the President meant to reduce the value of the dollar again, but the President smiled and shook his head. Some believe that the President's words indicate a desire to raise domestic prices without affecting the value of the dollar. The government has adopted two methods to adjust the domestic economic situation: first, to reduce debt; second, to raise prices. However, the President did not indicate to what extent prices must be raised, and at present, due to the drought and the Agricultural Adjustment Administration's plan, food prices have risen very quickly, but other items are still slightly behind. (National Telegram, 6th)

(Special Dispatch, 7th)

A Report on the Northwest Inspection

— Special correspondent for this newspaper, Geng Ya

An Overview of the Changes and Turmoil in Xinjiang This Year (6)

The new government of Xinjiang, born after the April 12th coup, will soon be celebrating its second anniversary. Looking back at the past year and a half, it can be said that it has been constantly battered. Now, the new government's new life has gradually improved. That is, the control of political and military power by Governor Sheng Shicai alone has become increasingly consolidated. However, the new government's ability to gain this new life can be said to have come from so-called "difficult creation, tragic management." Since its birth, the new government has not only had a major adversary in Ma Zhongying, who fought with it for more than a year, but also the internal strife among the central figures of the new government has been one wave after another. As for the ephemeral, almost twin-born independent government of Southern Xinjiang, its small history worthy of exploration has not yet been written. The Southern Xinjiang Hui people, Temir, and others suddenly raised the flag of an independent government in Kashgar. The news spread within China about its self-generation and self-destruction, which was inconsistent. However, the Hui people in Hami who had previously communicated with them said, "The establishment of the government is intended to achieve the goal of self-government by the people of Xinjiang under the guidance of the central government. The leader of the government, Timur, once said, 'A young colt that is not yet strong suddenly leaves home and escapes. If it encounters a wolf, it will undoubtedly have its lips greased. It is known that the people of Xinjiang still cannot completely leave the embrace and support of the central government and seek a dangerous path to survival.' Therefore, the new copper coins cast by the government are printed with the Kuomintang emblem, and the new flags erected also bear the Chinese national flag. This is not a false rumor. The attitude and meaning of the government can be clearly understood here." The government was destroyed long ago. The details of the process have been seen in various newspapers. Now, listening to the above, one can gain a better understanding of the general situation.

Yang Zengxin said that the ancient saying "There are no old friends west of Yangguan" should change the word "old" to "good". The new people also said that the new provincial rule is a paradise in times of peace and a deadly place in times of chaos. The former is Yang's many years of experience in governing Xinjiang, and the latter is derived from observing the geography. Both have their own objective appropriateness. It can be seen that the personnel in Xinjiang are complex and the environment is special, which cannot be compared with the inland. The aforementioned changes in the mountainous areas and the war with Sheng Ma, as well as the truth about the repeated infighting among the important figures in the new government, all seem unable to escape its criteria.

In addition to the internal strife within the new government, in June 1933, Tao Mingyue, Li Xiaotian, Chen Zhong, and others brewed the so-called "Second Coup," which has been mentioned in previous articles. After that, two major anti-Sheng organizations continued to be exposed. Most of the people engaged in this activity were close confidants of Sheng who had kinship with him. The president of the new government, Liu Wenlong, was also among them, which is no wonder outsiders find it shocking. Even Sheng himself could not figure it out at first.

The first organization to expose the opposition to Sheng was in October 1933. The main members were Zheng Runcheng, the former leader of the National Salvation Army (then the commander of the Dihua city defense), Yang Yaojun, the leader of the Self-Defense Army, Li Danchu, the director of the military factory, and Gmilek, the director of the Automobile Bureau, and twenty-five others. Liu Wenlong was among them. It was rumored that Liu had participated in the second coup by Tao, Li, and Chen. Upon hearing the news of Tao's execution, he turned pale for a long time. However, Liu and others were chairmen, and Sheng was not in a position to deal with them. He only tried to win over the converted troops that he had been raising. Liu had no way to deal with himself and politely asked Lian Lanpu to visit, but Sheng politely declined. This time, Liu participated again, knowing that Sheng had obtained clues, and secretly informed the mastermind's name first. Unexpectedly, Sheng issued a list, and Liu also impressively stamped it. Later, according to the list, all the people were imprisoned. The provincial government hastily announced that Liu had requested sick leave and was replaced by Zhu Fenglou, the director of the Department of Finance, as the acting chairman.

After Liu requested sick leave, he was initially placed under house arrest in the third hall of the provincial government, which was originally the residence of the former chairman Jin Shuren, with luxurious equipment and valuable objects worth more than 200,000 yuan. Jin fled alone, and Liu immediately moved in with his family. After the incident, the "Confiscated Property Clearance Committee" sent personnel to check the objects. Liu tried his best to resist and shouted while lying on the ground, "You are so unreasonable, are you trying to force me to my death?" However, he was finally forced to move back to his private residence. Liu had served in lucrative positions in eight cities in Southern Xinjiang and had a large fortune. He often engaged in commerce and lending. In Ili and Tacheng, he had 100,000 sheep. When Ma Zhongying was about to besiege Dihua, the public discussed quickly moving government grain into the city, but Liu opposed it to no avail. Later, when grain prices soared after the city was besieged, Liu calmly opened his private granary and sold it at a good price. He was so skilled at accumulating wealth that it was rumored that he had more than one million taels of silver at home, but they were all handled by the Clearance Committee. There were many other "confiscated properties" that were cleared, among which those of Jin Shuren (accumulated during Jin's five years in Xinjiang, mostly famous antiques), Tao Mingyue, Zhang Peiyuan, and Cui Zhaoji were the most abundant. The origin of their abundance was almost entirely from extortion. In addition, there were many Han officials and civilians who were victims of the Hui rebellions in various counties in Southern Xinjiang. However, according to those who escaped from the war, the truly honest and people-loving county magistrates were treated differently and were not all destroyed. Illicit gains come with illicit losses. There is an ancient saying that those who govern the people should know how to conduct themselves.

In the first half of 1934, most of the troops were sent to Southern Xinjiang to clean up the remnants of Ma and suppress various things. Sheng himself did not leave Dihua lightly, and it was still peaceful and uneventful. However, in September, Su Shangda, the general manager of the New Xinjiang Bank, who was known as the "Second Governor," was suddenly arrested and imprisoned, and the atmosphere suddenly became tense again. Those who were implicated included Jin, a section chief of the Department of Construction, Liu, the director of the Automobile Bureau, Chen, the captain of the Boy Scout team, and six others. The details of the case have not yet been announced. There are various rumors circulating outside. Some say that Su and others secretly bought guns and plotted to assassinate Sheng, and the matter was leaked. Some say that this was the result of a secret struggle between the two factions of those who studied in Japan (Sheng's representative) and those who studied in the United States (Su's representative). According to Wang Guoguang, the director of the Radio Station, Sheng and Su had a close personal friendship, but they had different political views, which forced them to take this action. However, no matter what, they were both anti-Sheng.

Looking at the New Xinjiang April 12th Coup, the execution of Tao, Li, and Chen, Liu Wenlong's house arrest, Zhang Peiyuan's attack on the provincial government, and Su Shangda's arrest, the new people constantly mentioned them together and called them the "Five Revolutions." When the fifth incident was exposed, the current chairman Li Rong (Zhu Fenglou had already resigned) discussed with Sheng about issuing passports to Shanxi so that dissidents could leave at their own convenience. For a time, officials and civilians enthusiastically applied for passports. The last time, three new Sui automobiles departed directly from Dihua eastward (after which they would travel from Sui to Hami). Tickets were sold out a dozen days ago. On the way from Dihua to Hami, the Kazakhs killed and robbed people. From Dihua to Turpan, the short journey of six stations cost 200,000 taels of paper money to hire a cart (approximately 400 yuan in current currency), but no one dared to accept the order. In the area of Qijiaojing east of the road, one had to hire a Kazakh soldier to escort them. There were even fewer people riding camels. Before long, the order to stop issuing passports was issued again. Therefore, those who were able to return to Hami rejoiced with the phrase "enter Yumen Pass alive."

At present, the internal situation in New Xinjiang is due to the fact that the strength of the opposition parties such as Ma Zhongying and Zhang Peiyuan has been eliminated one after another, and the new provincial government has given priority to employing the leaders of various ethnic groups (especially the Hui people), such as the vice chairman of the provincial government, the vice directors of various departments, the administrative chiefs of various districts, and the division and brigade commanders of the governor's office, all of whom are from various ethnic groups, which is able to appease people's hearts. On the anniversary of the April 12th Revolution, Sheng said, "The situation in New Xinjiang is special. Only when the military plan is realized can political guarantees be achieved." Now, generally speaking, the new authorities have indeed managed to end the military and concentrate power. From now on, if they are not affected by external forces or unexpected changes, and on the one hand, they work harder to build and attach importance to the interests of various ethnic groups, then the future is immeasurable.

Zhu and Mao Trapped in Zunyi; Xu Bandit Front Also Wavering

Hankou Communication: Zhu De, Mao Zedong, Peng Dehuai, and other remnant bandits fled westwards to the Yunnan border some time ago, attempting to break into Leibo and Ebian counties, occupy western Sichuan, threaten Chengdu if they advanced, and use it as a base for rest. However, the Yunnan army strictly blocked them at the junction of Weixin and Zhenxiong, inflicting heavy casualties on the bandits, who then fled back to the border of Sichuan and Guizhou. The bandits, after wandering through several provinces, were exhausted. They initially intended to cross the Jinsha River to connect with the Xu bandits in northern Sichuan. Having failed to pass through Yunnan, they had no choice but to change their plans and cross the Wu River southward to join forces with the He bandits in western Hunan. The bandit suppression troops, aware of their intentions, defended the Wu River line while launching a joint encirclement. At the beginning of this month, the bandits fled to Zhongzhuang and Huangnipu near Zunyi, and the situation in northern Guizhou became tense again. However, as the bandits arrived in Zunyi, various armies followed closely. The National Army advanced rapidly in three routes and has surrounded the bandits. A portion of them fled to Suiyang, attempting to break through to Meitan and Fengquan, but the Wu River blocked their path, making it impossible to escape into Hunan. At this time, the He Long and Xiao Ke bandits also broke out of Dayong, fleeing westwards to Yuanling and Luxi, intending to meet Zhu and Mao. However, the National Army's defense line was solid, preventing them from passing through. The Hunan and Hubei armies redoubled their efforts to suppress them, making it possible to annihilate these bandits. He Jian, the commander-in-chief of the first route of pursuit and suppression, originally departed from Hunan on the 2nd to come to Hankou to meet Chiang Kai-shek and seek instructions. However, hearing that Chiang Kai-shek had gone to Chongqing, he turned back to Changsha and went directly to Changde to supervise the suppression. After He and Xiao are cleared, he will lead a large army into Guizhou to pursue them. When the Xu Zhang and other bandits in northern Sichuan were under the second general suppression by the Sichuan army, internal strife had already occurred. The military faction, including Xu Xiangqian, advocated defending Tongnan, Ba, Cangxi, and Yi counties, taking Jiange in the north, and eyeing Suining in the south. The political faction, including Zhang Guotao, advocated abandoning northern Sichuan and fleeing to Shaanxi and Gansu. Subsequently, the Zhang bandits fled north to Guangyuan and Nanzheng without success, and the Xu bandits also lost Tong, Ba, Cang, and Yi. All plans failed. Currently, the bandits only occupy a corner of Nanjiang in Sichuan and no more than Ningqiang County in Shaanxi. The bandit front initially stretched from east to west, but now it has changed to from south to . After the recovery of Mian County, the bandits on the front line suffered heavy blows.

And the side of the bandit front, again because of the National Army attack and wavering, according to Deng Xihou telegrams, that route Yang Rong Xiang Shi Feng Brigade, the 3rd to Chenjiaba attack, in Junjia E Mao Ezi with the bandits pseudo 20th Army 21st Army encountered, fierce battle five hours, at the same time Li Brigade out of Daba Pass, occupied Goujia Factory Stone Emen Branch Guoshi, the bandit was unable to support, then the whole line of retreat Hengliangzi Chaotianyi, and the pontoon bridge was burned down, blocking Deng's army attack, to the Nanjiang front, the bandits still garrison Wangcang Dam with the main force, there is no fierce fighting, Chiang Kai-shek has arrived in Chongqing, within days will convene Sichuan Guizhou generals, personally taught strategy, limited period to clear all bandits, so intends to temporarily stay in Chongqing, in order to command, Secretary-General Yang Yongtai, the 4th has been summoned to Sichuan, to assist everything, stationed in Hubei pacification Lord He Chengjun, also got Chiang telegram summons to go, early Jie and Yang to travel together, because of things stopped, about two or three days, that is, from Hankou to start, (March 5)

Anhui Construction Department Plans to Repair Three Major Water Conservancy Projects – Huayang River, Shao Weir, Chaohu Lake –

Anqing Communication: In order to prevent the backflow of river water in the Huayang River area, and to connect the Shao Weir and dredge Chaohu Lake, the Anhui Provincial Construction Department plans to launch the Huayang River Area Consolidation Project, the Diversion Project, and the Chaohu Lake Dredging Project. All the plans have been drafted and are being actively prepared. Construction will begin soon. The following is a summary of the plan:

(A) The Huayang River Water Conservancy Area covers more than 8,000 square kilometers, spanning the jurisdictions of Hubei, Anhui, and Jiangxi provinces, with Anhui province accounting for the majority. The people of this province have suffered disasters repeatedly. Since the beginning of the Republic of China, they have jointly conducted consolidation movements with Hubei and Jiangxi provinces. Subsequently, the central government sent personnel to supervise the project, with Anhui province as the main body. Due to insufficient funding, no achievements have been made. This province, based on repeated requests from the people, continued to raise funds for consolidation. After organizing a survey team for measurement and design, it was confirmed that the cost was not much, but the benefits were enormous. It is estimated that after consolidation, the following can be obtained: (1) 1.1 million mu of dried fields, estimated at 15 yuan per mu, worth 16.5 million yuan; (2) 298,000 mu of benefited fields, with an estimated increase of 5 yuan per mu, worth 1.49 million yuan. The total value of both items is 17.99 million yuan. The increase in agricultural production for the people and the increase in tax revenue for the government are not included. The construction methods are: (1) Construction of a 200-meter-long earth dam; (2) Construction of three reinforced concrete culverts; (3) Construction of one ship lock; (4) Dredging of internal river channels; (5) Construction of dikes around the lake; (6) Construction of bank protection works connecting the river dikes to the gate; (7) Repair of the Ma Hua Dike. The total cost of the project is estimated to be 1.022974 million yuan. The seventh item, the Ma Hua Dike, has already been repaired, which can save 150,000 yuan, so the remaining amount is 1.872974 million yuan. It is divided into three phases to implement. The first phase will first implement items one, three, four, and three, requiring 542,917 yuan.

(B) The Shao Weir in Shouxian County, northern Anhui, was created in the Spring and Autumn period. It is said by Chu Prime Minister Sun Shuao, as an ancient famous water conservancy area. Its operation is earlier than the Northwest Qin Canal, Han Canal, Zheng Canal, and Bai Canal. Initially, it irrigated 1 million mu, or said to be 4 million mu. Over time, it gradually became obsolete. Today, only more than 100,000 mu of irrigation area remain. Its water source is one to draw water from the Pi River and the other to receive mountain water. Due to the blockage of the diversion route, the irrigation area is shrinking day by day. The Anhui Provincial Government is seeking to restore the old view and sent personnel to survey and design it. Its construction methods are: A. Dredge the bottom of the channel that diverts the Pi River to one meter below the low water level, the channel bottom is four meters wide, and build a flood control gate; B. Dredge the channel bottom to half a meter below the low water level, two meters wide, and extend the original spillway dam. Type A requires an engineering fee of 121,231 yuan, and Type B requires 61,043 yuan. It is now proposed to adopt the Type A method and allocate funds for implementation.

(C) Chaohu Lake is located in the hinterland of Anhui Province, with an area of 2,800 square kilometers. It collects water from counties such as He, Chao, Shu, and Lu, with a vast basin of about 10,000 square kilometers. It borders the long Huai River in the north and the big Yangtze River in the south. Its main waterway carries the first heavy town of Hefei in the upstream, passes through Shikou, Chaoxian, Yunchao, and reaches Hexian's Yuxikou to enter the river. Its important tributaries take the route from Sanhe Town upstream to towns such as Fengle, Xincang, and Taoxi, reaching Shucheng and Lu'an. The agricultural water conservancy around the lake for hundreds is extremely important. The output of grain, tea, hemp and other items from Lu'an, Hefei and other all take this road. Since the blockage of the lake entrance, the traffic is blocked bricks, its Shikou one place, there is a very large silt beach, across the lake mouth, winter water dry, Heng with cattle dragging ships, is very inconvenient. Its construction plan is to dredge from Zhongmiao via Shikou to Hefei County, about 55 kilometers long. Inside (1) Zhongmiao to Shikou section of 20 kilometers, the average dredging depth of 2 meters, about 560,000 cubic meters of excavation, with dredger excavation, (2) Shikou to Hefei section of thirty-five kilometers, the average dredging depth of 1 meter, about 300,000 cubic meters of excavation, the first section of dredger excavation, each cubic meter to 1.5 cents, the need for 84,000 yuan, the second section of artificial excavation, each cubic meter to 1 dime, the need for 30,000 yuan, two together need 114,000 yuan.

The above plan has recently been resolved at the Standing Committee of the Provincial Government, allocating 100,000 shi of relief rice and 160,000 yuan of relief funds, and choosing to do urgent work to relieve disasters. It is heard that the Provincial Government has decided to allocate 1,700 shi of relief rice and 10,000 yuan of construction funds to the Pi River, allocate 2,500 shi of relief rice and 50,000 yuan of construction funds to Chaohu Lake, and allocate 2,000 shi of relief rice and 100,000 yuan of construction funds to the Huayang River, which will be handled separately by the Construction Department in order to complete them. (March 5)

Japanese Purchase and Transport of Qin and Han Bricks and Tiles Case Concluded - The Entire Value Is No Less Than a City - Compensation for the Price Settled Locally

Jinan Communication: Shandong is the land of Qilu, the birthplace of Confucius and Mencius, so the influence of culture and the ethos of customs have all taken the lead. Therefore, the literary style of past generations is luxuriant. In the past, during times of peace, most of the reading seeds were devoted to the collection of antiques, concentrating on textual research to show their erudition. Passing on and learning, it became a trend. For example, the Haiyuan Pavilion's collection of books in Liaocheng, the Great Sutra of Nanhai Temple in Yexian, and the bricks and tiles of Wan Yin in Weixian, although they initially arose from temporary interests, are deeply related to the culture and history of our country. It is a great pity that their descendants could not inherit the legacy of their predecessors, cherish and treasure them, and collude with foreigners due to domestic unscrupulous merchants, dazzled by high prices, and the great national treasure was lost and flowed into foreign lands, which is very lamentable. The Haiyuan Pavilion's collection of books and the treasures of Wanyinlou were damaged, sold, and no longer belonged to Shandong Province. The Qin and Han bricks and tiles were also extremely valuable. Unexpectedly, the descendants of the Gao family could not inherit the mantle of their predecessors. In mid-May of the twentieth year of the Republic of China, they sold all the bricks and tiles to Ota, a famous Japanese antique dealer. The introducer was a Mr. Gong. The selling price was only 2,500 yuan. Mr. Gong received 900 yuan, and the Gao family only received 1,600 yuan. With this small amount of money, they actually ruined the only national treasure. The representative of the Japanese acquisition was named Kuhara. He divided the bricks and tiles into five large boxes in Weixian and secretly transported them to Qingdao. They were shipped from May 17th of that year and arrived in Qing on the 18th. The matter was heard by the Shandong Provincial Library. They immediately telegraphed the Qingdao Municipal Government, the Education Bureau, the Social Bureau, and the Jiaoji Railway Administration, stating that the bricks and tiles were related to national culture and requested that they be detained in accordance with the Law on the Preservation of Antiquities. On the 22nd, a telegram was received from the Jiaoji Railway stating that the antiques transported by Ota were two steles and five boxes of Han bricks and tiles, which were indeed treasures and had been temporarily detained. The Education Department sent Wu Jingshou to Qingdao to negotiate so that the antiques could be transported back to Jinan, and telegraphed the Ministry of Education to report. When Wu arrived in Qingdao, he found out that two of the twelve-character bricks had been taken away by the Japanese, leaving only one and other bricks and tiles. He negotiated to transport them to Jinan. Unexpectedly, the Japanese Chief of the Traffic Department of the Jiaoji Railway, Kagasawa Manabu, refused. After repeated negotiations, the antiques were transported from Qing to Jinan on June 14th. On the 16th, the Provincial Government sent Secretary Ren Fenggang and Liu Runmin, together with Pi Songyun, Chief of the Third Section of the Education Department, and Wang Xiantang, Director of the Provincial Library, to be responsible for checking. A total of 531 bricks and tiles and two portraits were displayed in the library. The history of the bricks and tiles was originally that Gao Qingling, a collector of antiques in Weixian, Shandong Province in the Qing Dynasty, collected about seven or eight hundred pieces of Qin and Han bricks and tiles, which were the essence of the national ancient bricks and tiles and the only crystallization of the history of Chinese pottery culture. Gao wrote the book "Shang Tao Shi Bricks and Tiles Wen," to record the matter. The book has a total of 24 large volumes, all of which are rubbings, about two feet long and eight inches wide. The Shandong Provincial Library purchased one of them for 350 yuan. The most valuable brick and tile is the twelve-character brick, with the twelve characters "The sea is full of ministers, and the year is mature, and there is no hungry person." The brick is square, each side is eight inches long, and it is placed in a wooden box. The text on the box is written by Wang Yirong, which reads, "The twelve characters are all special words, obtained by Hansheng, and ordered to be made in the Qin Dynasty. Weng Ge Xue said that the era is determined by the text, and he is about to use this sentence to celebrate the current Tianjia. Yi Rong Ji," Gao Hansheng was the son of Gao Qingling, and he wrote a poem attached to it. The value of all the bricks and tiles is no less than a city of jade.

After the bricks and tiles were detained, the Japanese negotiated repeatedly, and the Japanese ambassador negotiated with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of our country. After a delay of four years, the Provincial Government received two telegrams from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Dongshi, ordering the case to be quickly settled locally through consultation, and the settlement of the case was reported for record. The Provincial Government ordered the Education Department to review and report. After the Education Department, in accordance with the claims of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, drafted measures and submitted them to the Provincial Government for approval. It was then submitted to the Political Affairs Conference on the 5th and resolved. The original text of the Education Department's proposal is copied below, "The Education Department presented that it received two telegrams from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Dongshi, regarding the case of Japanese nationals purchasing Gao's antiques in Weixian being detained, ordering that the case be quickly settled locally through consultation in accordance with the method of compensating for the price, and the settlement of the case be reported to the Ministry for record, etc. Upon receiving this, it was found that this case is related to foreign affairs, and it seems that the Provincial Government can send personnel to consult with the Japanese Consul stationed in Jinan in accordance with the claims of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and give the original purchaser a considerable amount of compensation based on the transaction price of 2,500 yuan for the antiques, so as to settle the case. The reason for submitting this for approval is to ask for a public decision," (5th)

Rice Industry Association Changes to New Measuring Instruments

The county's Rice Industry Association convened an executive meeting yesterday. The chairman, Zhang Jiliang, decided that the industry would switch to the new measurement system. The county government has repeatedly ordered them to do so. They all believed that neighboring counties had already switched. Therefore, it was decided to implement it on March 16, and the measuring instruments were checked on the 13th and 14th. The association will first prepare standard measuring instruments. The price of measuring instruments, except for the price of one-dou measuring instruments, will be calculated after production. One-sheng measuring instrument costs 4.8 cents per unit, plus a 2-cent inspection fee. There are no restrictions on the import of foreign rice, which is destroying domestic agriculture. The meeting agreed to send a telegram to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance and Industry to strictly supervise and increase import tariffs to maintain agriculture.

Suzhou Youth Commits Suicide in Wuxi

Zhu Xianzhang from outside Kuatang, Suzhou, was 26 years old. His father, Peidao, died many years ago. His uncle, Peiran, opened Tiancheng Tung Oil Bank in Suzhou. Because he had no heirs, Xianzhang took over both families and Peiran married him to a woman named Li. He had two children each. However, Xianzhang liked to spend money lavishly and spent more than 4,000 yuan in three months, resulting in a debt-ridden situation. Peiran refused to take care of it for him. Xianzhang felt unable to make up for it and developed a pessimistic attitude towards life. He came to Wuxi the day before yesterday afternoon and stayed in room 67 of the Wuxi Hotel. That night, he wrote a letter, gave it to the waiter to mail, and then closed the door and slept peacefully. At about 9:00 am yesterday, Xianzhang had not yet gotten up. The waiter called him but did not respond, so he climbed through the window and saw him lying face up on the bed, his face pale, dying. He knew he had taken poison and was rushed to Tongren Hospital for treatment. He eventually died of poisoning at midnight. Wuxi Hotel sent a special person to Suzhou to notify his family to come to Wuxi to take care of the aftermath. On the one hand, Xi Zhiliang, the head of Tian San Tu, reported to the court for an autopsy.

Kong Xiangxi Returned to Shanghai from Nanjing Yesterday: Discussed the Shenxin Affair, Methods Under Study; International Loans Also Gladly Supported

Central News Agency reports: Kong Xiangxi, Vice President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, returned to Shanghai from Nanjing yesterday morning. The reporter first inquired about his trip to Wuhan, and he said that he went to Wuhan to meet with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek regarding the compilation of the 24th year budget. The military expenditure portion required further discussion. Also, due to the urgency of suppressing military affairs, it was necessary to build highways in four provinces, and to discuss the financial problems of provinces using troops such as Sichuan and Guizhou. Finally, when asked about international loans, he said that since the global economic downturn and the United States' implementation of the silver purchase policy, China's silver had been flowing out considerably, and the social finance had been affected by this. The market had lost its usual vitality. China, as the largest market in the East, had caused international commerce to be affected as well. Various friendly nations, considering the benefits of their trade, deeply hoped that the market would stabilize as soon as possible, so they had a strong desire to provide assistance. The people of our society, on their part, greatly hoped that the government, in order to rescue our social economy and stabilize the financial market, would also gladly support it. Today is International Women's Day: Two Women's Organizations Hold Grand Commemorations

Letter to Women

International Women's Day Letter to Women, Dear Sisters, Time passes quickly, it is again "March 8th" (omitted) Since "September 18th" to this day, China is fragmented, the countryside is bankrupt, externally there is strong aggression, internally there are continuous wars, Japanese imperialism, in addition to its military aggression, is rapidly carrying out its economic aggression against China, in order to fulfill its dream of a continental policy, China, increasingly ruined by colonialism, is about to step onto the final stage of being completely devoured or jointly managed. In other words, the fate of the Chinese nation is on the verge of life and death. Women cannot exist independently from the nation, nor can they seek solutions to their own problems independently from the nation's survival. Therefore, Chinese women, in addition to struggling for their own liberation, should also strive for the national liberation movement. "March 8th" is a day when women around the world jointly seek liberation. In the eyes of women who have already been liberated, it is good news, and the formal commemoration is, of course, a celebration. However, in the eyes of Chinese women under heavy oppression, it can only be a warning sign, and the expression that comes with this warning sign is the spirit of going to war and the determination to resist. Sisters, rise up together, unite closely, continue the spirit of the enlightened and strive, shoulder the unfinished mission of our predecessors, resist feudal forces, overthrow imperialism, and promote women's liberation, human equality, and world peace. Respectfully issued by the Shanghai Women's Association.
