Order of the Meeting

The association is scheduled to hold the meeting starting at 2:00 PM today. However, in order to connect the feelings of women from various countries, it plans to hold a luncheon in advance to welcome women from all walks of life to participate. The number of people who have registered is extremely enthusiastic. After the meal, the commemorative meeting will be held immediately. The order of events is as follows: (1) Ringing the bell to open the meeting; (2) Performing the rituals; (3) The presidium reports the purpose of the meeting; (4) Offering flowers and paying tribute to the women martyrs of various countries; (5) Speeches; (6) Discussion of proposals; (7) Distribution of commemorative special issues; (8) Adjournment.

Distribution of Special Issues

In addition, in order to make all circles understand the meaning of the women's movement, a large volume of special issues has been published, including Zhang Mojun's "Thoughts on the March 8th" festival, He Xiangning's open letter, Chen Lingyi's "Balance Sheet for the March 8th" festival, Yang Zhihao's "Reviewing the Women's Movement in China's Past from this Year's March 8th" festival, Chen Yongsheng's "Several Things that Women Must Strive to Promote This Year," Wang Liming's "Sisters, Forward, Forward," and Shi Liang, Guo Zhenyi, Chen Fengxi, and others, as well as works by other female writers.

Meeting of the Banking Joint Reserve Committee: Record of the Delegates' Meeting of the Member Banks; Report on Last Year's Business and Election of New Executive Committee; Preparation Enrichment and Exchange Show Significant Progress

The Shanghai Banking Association's Joint Reserve Committee has been established for three years. The committee has been handling joint reserves and bill exchange affairs, and in the past year, it has made significant progress. At 4:00 PM on the 6th of this month, the annual meeting of the member banks' delegates was held. The executive committee reported on the business situation for the 23rd year, and the conference re-elected the fourth executive committee and the third clearing house committee. The above-mentioned report and the list of elected members are listed separately below.

This Year's Members

The eleven elected executive committee members are: Mr. Li Fucun, Mr. Tang Shoumin, Mr. Bei Songsun, Mr. Xu Jilu, Mr. Qian Xinzhi, Mr. Chen Guangfu, Mr. Ye Fuxiao, Mr. Chen Zeqing, Mr. Hu Bijiang, Mr. Wu Yunqi, and Mr. Sun Hengfu. After the conference that day, the executive committee meeting was held, and five standing committee members were elected by mutual vote. Mr. Li Fucun, Mr. Bei Songsun, Mr. Tang Shoumin, Mr. Xu Jilu, and Mr. Qian Xinzhi were elected. Then, the standing committee members elected a chairman by mutual vote. Mr. Li Fucun was elected. All of the above gentlemen were re-elected this year. The nine elected clearing house members for this year are: Mr. Cheng Muhao, Mr. Chen Mutang, Mr. Yang Jemei, Mr. Su Fuxiao, Mr. Chen Duoru, Mr. Wang Boyuan, Mr. Zhou Desun, Mr. Wang Zihou, and Mr. Liu Hongyuan. Also, there were no changes in the Chinese and Western members of the association's evaluation and custody teams this year.

Business Report

At the beginning of the 23rd year, Shanghai's silver deposits were as abundant as before. Weekly warehouse inspection reports showed increasing silver, seemingly indicating prosperity. However, examining the source, most of it was the price paid for purchasing foreign goods from the interior. Because the income from production was not enough to offset it, it was necessary to transport silver to Shanghai. The relaxation of Shanghai's finances was a reflection of the financial depletion of the interior. In other words, every province, county, town, village was importing more than exporting. Once silver arrived in Shanghai, part of it was no longer owned by Chinese people. However, before leaving the country, it could still be a medium for domestic transactions, but it had the opportunity to drift away at any time. Our industry colleagues silently observed such a twisted form of relaxation and decided that it could not last. On the one hand, we tried to develop properly, and on the other hand, we always strictly guarded against the onslaught of panic. Since summer and autumn, droughts have spread everywhere, and the source of the interior has dried up. Suddenly, the United States vigorously implemented its silver purchase bill, and overseas silver prices soared. By purchasing silver in Shanghai and reselling it in overseas markets, substantial profits could be obtained. In a few months, there was a large outflow, causing panic and a sudden tightening of credit. Later, the government levied a silver tax to make it unprofitable, and the government declared the rumors of inflation to be untrue, and people's hearts were roughly settled. Our industry colleagues, in this environment, still adhered to their prudent approach and deep solidarity, and were able to maintain their modest prosperity. Whether China's economy can improve in the future depends entirely on the state of international payments. Whether silver deposits flow out or not is a secondary issue. How should we contribute to the government, guide society, rescue the countryside, and assist industry and commerce so that the amount of imports gradually decreases to balance? Our industry colleagues must have been preparing thoroughly. This is what the committee is waiting to see. The committee has been established for three years, and thanks to the supervision of colleagues, we have been able to avoid failures. In addition to maintaining the enrichment of the reserve portion, there has also been significant development in other exchange affairs. Now that it is the end of the 23rd year, we respectfully report the key points of the business situation of the past year as follows.

Joint Reserves

(A) Joint Reserve Section: (1) Admission of New Member Banks: In February of this year, Hengli Bank joined the committee as a member bank. (2) Reserve Assets: The total amount of reserve assets deposited by each bank, according to the total amount of the year-end settlement this year, is 60,071,912.04 silver dollars. The total amount of all reserves was 66.78% of the total evaluated amount in the previous settlement period and 62.91% in the next settlement period. Asset classification, according to the number of the next settlement period, real estate accounts for 85.32% of the total, foreign securities account for 9.65%, and domestic public bonds account for 5.02%. This year, there were not many real estate transactions in Shanghai. Real estate is the main part of the association's reserve assets. In the future, adjustments should be made as appropriate, seeking agility in verification. (3) Various Documents and Interbank Discount Loans: The documents received by each bank are still used to deposit various reserves or are exercised among colleagues. At the beginning of this year, the financial situation was relaxed as described above. The average interest rate for public bond loans from the association in the first half of the year was 9%, and the average discount rate was 12%. Since August, credit has tightened sharply, and the interest rate for interbank loans has gradually increased. In December, it rose sharply. On December 28, the interest rate for money shops rose to 60%. The interest rate for the association's public bond loans was 30%, and the discount rate was 34%. Throughout the year, the total amount of loans borrowed from the association by each bank was only more than 2.7 million yuan. The abundance of the strength of our colleagues can be seen in general. The public bond discount item has not been implemented this year. (4) Exchange Deposits: The average exchange deposits of exchange banks were higher in the first half of the year. Since November in the second half of the year, due to the reduction of silver deposits in the city, the amount of deposits has also decreased accordingly. The total amount of year-end deposits totaled 10,024,000 silver dollars, of which silver dollars accounted for 51.91% and remittances accounted for 48.09%. The ratio of the exchange difference to the exchange deposit averaged 1/31.05. Profits and Losses: This year, in accordance with the resolution of the 10th Delegates' Meeting of Member Banks, appropriate loans were made to ensure guarantees. The interest income was used as the association's operating fund. The total income from loan interest for the whole year was 121,653.85 yuan and the total from interbank lending was 461.11 yuan, for a total of 122,114.96 silver dollars. The budget for the reserve portion was 18,000 yuan. The amount of the final account was 18,292.37 yuan, which was 292.37 yuan higher than the budget, a decrease of 20% compared to the previous year. After amortizing equipment and start-up costs, the net profit was 94,910.57 silver dollars after offsetting profits and losses.

Bill Exchange

(B) Bill Exchange Section: (1) Progress in the Scope of Exchange: On January 4 this year, Hengli Bank joined as an exchange bank. Sichuan Meifeng Bank entrusted Xinhua Bank to act as an exchange agent from the same day. On August 1, Chouye Bank and Jiangzhe Commercial Savings Bank simultaneously joined as exchange banks. There are 15 new branches in the city that have joined the exchange one after another. In addition, the number of silver money shops in the city entrusting exchange banks to collect bills has also increased. According to the latest survey, there are more than 150 shops. (2) Exchange Volume: The total exchange volume for the whole year was 322,211,609.54 silver dollars, an increase of 64% over the previous year, and 1,627,784 bills, an increase of 80% over the previous year. The average daily exchange volume was 10,070,400 silver dollars and 5,400 bills. Comparing the monthly exchange amounts, the daily average in January, April, and May was all above 9 million yuan, the same as the highest month of the previous year, but the lowest this year. February, June, and July were all above 10 million yuan. August to November were all above 11 million yuan. By December, the daily average reached 13 million yuan, the highest record since the exchange was established. The ratio of the total exchange difference to the total exchange, calculated by combining silver dollars and remittance silver dollars, averaged 14.80%. (3) Exchange Expenses: The budget for the exchange portion of the year was 52,000 yuan. The final account was 51,298.59 yuan, a decrease of 701.41 yuan compared to the budget. Calculated according to the total amount of exchange receipts and payments for the whole year, the cost is only 7.9 li per thousand yuan of exchange bills, a decrease of 3 li compared to the previous year. In order to exempt the burden on each bank, it is proposed to pay it from the association's net profit. Executive Committee: Li Fucun (Chairman), Bei Songsun (Standing Committee Member), Tang Shoumin (Standing Committee Member), Qian Xinzhi (Standing Committee Member), Xu Jilu (Duty Committee Member), Chen Guangfu, Chen Zeqing, Wu Yunzai, Hu Bijiang, Ye Fuxiao, Sun Hengfu. Manager: Zhu Boquan. Deputy Manager: Xu Baoqi. Assistant Manager: Bao Cheng.

The China Industry and Commerce Relief Association Decided on Relief Measures for Industry and Commerce: Divided into Credit Small Loans and Mortgage Loans on Goods; Total Amount is 5 Million and 10 Million Yuan Respectively

Guowen News Agency reports: The China Industry and Commerce Relief Association, organized by leaders in industry and commerce throughout the city, has repeatedly discussed relief plans for industry and commerce since its inception. It has also appointed representatives to negotiate with Mr. Zhang Gongquan, a leader in the banking industry. It is now known that the plan drafted by the association is divided into two types: one is a credit small loan, and the other is a mortgage loan on assessed goods. The methods have been decided and sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, local associations, and Mr. Zhang Gongquan, a leader in the banking industry, so that they can be effectively implemented. The details of each are recorded as follows:

Letter to Zhang Gongquan

Mr. Gongquan Jianjian, Respectfully, yesterday, I was very admired that you had agreed to have the two directors of our association, Wu Zhihao and Zhang Zilian, study various methods to relieve industry and commerce and cooperate fully to overcome difficulties. Among the agreed methods, two items will be carried out first: (1) Credit small loans to relieve small industry and commerce; (2) Mortgage loans on publicly assessed goods to relieve industrial and commercial firms. The specific methods are intended to be discussed mutually by representatives appointed by both parties. Today, Mr. Wu Zhihao will tell you in person that you have appointed two representatives, which shows your enthusiasm for relieving industry and commerce. I am very grateful. Please schedule a meeting so that our association can also discuss and appoint representatives with the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to discuss the specific methods in person to facilitate the implementation. This is respectfully sent to you, and another letter to Zhang Gongquan says: Mr. Gongquan Jianjian, Respectfully, regarding the relief methods for industry and commerce, our association directors Wu Zhihao and Zhang Zilian had previously discussed with you once and decided that representatives should be appointed by both parties to discuss specific methods together. Many days have passed, and there has been no definite news. Now, I am especially sending you the two kinds of programs determined by our meeting, and I hope that you will reply concretely within three days and hold the meeting on schedule to relieve the difficulties of the merchants and the distress of the people. All 3.5 million industrial, commercial, and civilian citizens of Shanghai are eagerly awaiting, and this is what is hoped for. This is to wish you well.

Credit Small Loans

Methods for Small Industrial and Commercial Credit Loans: (1) This loan shall be handled by a syndicate organized by the Bank of China; (2) The total amount of credit small loans is 5 million yuan of national currency; (3) All small and medium-sized industrial and commercial stores or factories operating with Chinese capital within the Shanghai area may apply for credit loans upon review and approval by the association in accordance with the following conditions: (A) The capital is more than 10,000 yuan; (B) There are two stores or factories with the same capital to provide joint and several guarantees; (4) The amount of each credit small loan shall not exceed three-tenths of its total capital at most; (5) The repayment period of credit small loans shall be six months after the date of the loan and shall be repaid in installments, up to a maximum of one year; (6) Anyone who wants to apply for a credit small loan should apply to the China Industry and Commerce Relief Association in writing within one month from the date of the loan syndicate's formation, and state the amount of the loan and the license number and capital amount of the joint and several guarantor, in duplicate. After review and approval by the China Industry and Commerce Relief Association, one copy will be sent to the syndicate for further investigation. After one month, the syndicate shall, together with the China Industry and Commerce Relief Association, count the total amount of loan requests, and if the total amount of loans does not exceed the total amount of 5 million yuan and there is no violation of the conditions stipulated in Article 3, the loan shall be implemented immediately; (7) After the expiration of the loan application period, if the application amount of loan applicants who meet the loan conditions after investigation exceeds the total loan amount of 5 million yuan, the loans shall be granted in proportion to the loans that meet the conditions and the total loan amount of 5 million yuan; (8) The interest on this loan shall not exceed 6% at the highest; (9) If a credit small loan is not repaid on time, the borrower goes bankrupt, or the joint and several guarantor is unable to repay, the loan syndicate shall be responsible for recovering the debt according to law.

Mortgage Method on Goods

Methods for Mortgage Loans on Publicly Assessed Goods: (1) The fixed amount for mortgage loans on publicly assessed goods is 10 million yuan. The following goods may be mortgaged: (A) Factory buildings, mortgaged at 70% of the original cost; (B) Factory base, publicly assessed by the public assessment committee and mortgaged at 80%; (C) Factory machinery, equipment, and wheel-transported ships are mortgaged at the depreciated price of the original purchase price; (D) Real estate with existing buildings is mortgaged according to the rental income, but the rental income shall not be lower than 5% compared to the mortgage interest; (The above-mentioned mortgage of houses is limited to those that conform to the relief and industrial use, but the total number of mortgages shall also not exceed one-third of the total); (E) Manufactured goods are mortgaged at 80% of the actual wholesale price; (2) The valuation of the above-mentioned mortgaged goods shall be publicly assessed by the goods public assessment committee. In addition to the representatives of the China Industry and Commerce Relief Association, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Local Association, and the mortgagee syndicate as ex officio members, the organization of the public assessment committee shall also hire experts from each industry, five in each industry, to jointly organize. When evaluating, the relevant expert members shall be invited to join according to their type and nature (the above committee members shall first determine the attending members and draw lots temporarily); (3) Anyone who wants to apply for a mortgage loan on goods should apply to the China Industry and Commerce Relief Association in writing within one month from the date of the loan syndicate's formation, and state the amount of the loan application and the name of the mortgaged goods, etc., in duplicate. After review and approval by the China Industry and Commerce Relief Association, one copy will be sent to the syndicate for further investigation. After one month, the syndicate shall, together with the China Industry and Commerce Relief Association, count the total amount of loan requests, and if the total amount of loans does not exceed the fixed amount of 10 million yuan and there is no violation of the conditions stipulated in Article 2, the loan shall be implemented immediately; (4) After the expiration of the mortgage loan application period, if the application amount of loan applicants who meet the loan conditions after investigation exceeds the total loan amount of 10 million yuan, the loans shall be granted in proportion to the loans that meet the conditions and the total loan amount of 10 million yuan; (5) The interest on this loan shall not exceed 6% at the highest; (6) The lending syndicate shall be responsible for promoting the unified financial control and issuing exchange coupons prepared with goods. This loan shall be transferred when the exchange coupons are issued, and the method shall be determined separately; (Mutual) In order to circulate the syndicate's finances, the syndicate shall organize a public goods depot and issue public documents to facilitate circulation. The syndicate shall formulate the methods and publish them for implementation together.

London Art Exhibition: British Commissioner to Arrive in Shanghai Tomorrow; Opening Date of Preview Exhibition Not Yet Confirmed

The preparatory work for the London Exhibition of Chinese Art, including the renovation of the former Bank of China building on Rue du Consulat (Ren Ji Lu), the inventory of ancient artifacts for the exhibition transported to Shanghai from the Cathedral Street (Tian Zhu Tang Jie) and various locations, as well as the undertaking of examination and safekeeping, has kept all staff members extremely busy. Yesterday, a reporter from the Central News Agency (Zhongyang She) visited Mr. Tang Xifen, the secretary of the exhibition, to inquire about the latest developments in the preparation and the confirmed date of the exhibition, as well as concerns raised by a certain academic group regarding the safety of transporting antiquities to England for the exhibition. The details are recorded below:

British Commissioner to Arrive in Shanghai

According to Mr. Tang, the London Exhibition of Chinese Art has dispatched a committee of five members to China specifically to select antiquities. Among them, Sir Percival David, the director-general of the exhibition, and Mr. Raphael have already arrived in Shanghai last month. They have also visited President Wang Jingwei and Education Minister Wang Shijie in Nanjing. They are scheduled to return to Shanghai today. In addition, Mr. Hobson and Mr. Oscar Raphael will arrive in Shanghai from Hong Kong tomorrow. Professor Paul Pelliot from France is expected to arrive on the 24th of this month.

Extremely Busy with Examination Work

Secretary Tang also stated that the examination and safekeeping committees of the exhibition, together with experienced artisans in handling antiquities, have been working in the warehouse for days to examine and safekeep the artifacts. Two photography experts have also been invited to film the selected artifacts for verification upon their return from the London exhibition and for the purpose of compiling a catalog. The total number of staff members involved is over forty. As for the confirmed date of the preview exhibition, there are varying rumors circulating. Some say it has been set for the 25th, but in reality, there is still no certainty on this end. This is because the procedures for examination and safekeeping are quite complex. Currently, efforts are being intensified in numbering and card-making, hoping to open the exhibition in the shortest possible time. It is expected to be realized around the 20th of this month. The duration of the exhibition will be approximately at least one month, but at most no more than forty days, as the venue here is scheduled for demolition in May.

Willing to Answer Questions on Security Concerns

The Central News Agency reporter then asked whether a certain academic group's concerns, recently reported in the newspapers, regarding the safety of transporting antiquities to England for the exhibition, had been addressed. Secretary Tang replied that they had not yet received any correspondence from the group. He added that he had just arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing, and that no such letters had been received in Nanjing either. However, the exhibition has always prioritized caution regarding the transportation of antiquities to England for the exhibition. Figures from various fields who are concerned about this issue, such as Mr. Tao Menghe from the North, had issued declarations as early as January and February, advocating for prudence in all matters. The exhibition has also provided essential explanations, which have been published in various newspapers. Perhaps some may not have noticed. The exhibition has formulated detailed regulations for the transportation of antiquities to England, which have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for record. The Palace Museum has also expressed its approval. If various sectors have any doubts regarding the safety of transporting antiquities to England, the exhibition is more than willing to provide detailed answers.

Rules of Procedure for the Preview Exhibition

Rules of Procedure for the Shanghai Preview Exhibition of the London Exhibition of Chinese Art: (1) The Preparatory Committee of the London Exhibition of Chinese Art International Exhibition, in order to demonstrate public trust, will hold a preview exhibition in Shanghai before the exhibition items leave the country. (2) The preview exhibition will be held at the former Bank of China building at No. 22 The Bund, Shanghai, and is scheduled to take place in March of the 24th year (1935). (3) The exhibition will have two executive directors, appointed by the director of the Preparatory Committee of the London Exhibition of Chinese Art (hereinafter referred to as the Director of the Preparatory Committee). They will be responsible for all affairs of the exhibition under the direction of the Director of the Preparatory Committee. (4) The exhibition will be divided into two sections, each with a director appointed by the Director of the Preparatory Committee, who will be responsible for all affairs of their respective sections under the direction of the Director of the Preparatory Committee and the executive directors. (5) Section One will be divided into the following divisions, each with several officers appointed by the executive directors in consultation with the Director of the Preparatory Committee. They will be responsible for the affairs of their respective divisions under the direction of the directors and executive directors. 1. Documentation Division: responsible for receiving, sending, drafting, writing, and filing official documents, recording meeting minutes, safeguarding official seals, and recording employee attendance. 2. General Affairs Division: responsible for purchasing and storing supplies, arranging and cleaning the office and exhibition venue, managing workers, providing meals and accommodation for exhibition staff, and handling matters not belonging to other divisions. 3. Accounting Division: responsible for cash receipts and disbursements, preparing budgets and final accounts, and preserving account books and receipts. 4. Editorial Division: responsible for editing exhibition publications, creating display item cards, and disseminating news. 5. Ticketing Division: responsible for printing, numbering, issuing, selling, and collecting admission tickets. 6. Reception Division: responsible for the reception of honorary staff and various social events at the exhibition venue and the exhibition. (6) Section Two will be divided into the following divisions, each with several officers appointed by the chairman. They will be responsible for the affairs of their respective divisions under the direction of the directors and executive directors. 1. Registration Division: responsible for registering solicited art items, creating labels and lists, and examining display records. 2. Custody Division: responsible for the inventory, return, and storage of art items, the safekeeping of art items at the venue, and the arrangement and supervision of custodial staff shifts. Detailed safekeeping measures will be determined separately. 3. Display Division: responsible for arranging the venue and displaying art items. 4. Security Division: responsible for patrolling, guarding, firefighting, and maintaining order in the warehouse, venue, office, and during transportation. (7) All staff members of the exhibition, from the executive directors downwards, shall be fully responsible for safekeeping duties, except for those with designated specific responsibilities. (8) The exhibition may appoint several honorary directors as necessary, to be appointed by the Director of the Preparatory Committee. (9) The exhibition may employ several Chinese and English clerks for writing documents, books, cards, and labels. (10) For important exhibition affairs, if deemed necessary, the Director of the Preparatory Committee or the executive directors may convene a meeting of the directors and the heads of the relevant divisions to make decisions. (11) If deemed necessary for the operation of section affairs, the directors of each section may convene a meeting of the section to make decisions. (12) Detailed rules of procedure for the exhibition and exhibition regulations will be determined separately.

Procedures for Inventory and Safekeeping

Procedures for Inventory and Safekeeping for the Shanghai Preview Exhibition of the London Exhibition of Chinese Art: (1) These procedures are formulated jointly by the Shanghai Office of the Palace Museum (hereinafter referred to as the Museum), the Shanghai Office of the Antiquities Exhibition Office of the Ministry of Interior (hereinafter referred to as the Exhibition Office), and the exhibition in accordance with Article □ of the Organizational Rules of the Shanghai Preview Exhibition of the London Exhibition of Chinese Art. (2) The procedures for the inventory of exhibition items are as follows: 1. The Museum and the Exhibition Office shall first classify and pack the items to be exhibited, affix seals, and then prepare two copies of the inventory list, one original and one duplicate, and transport them to the exhibition's warehouse. 2. During transportation, the Museum or the Exhibition Office and the exhibition (hereinafter referred to as both parties) shall designate escorts and assign guards to escort the items along the way. 3. When the items arrive at the warehouse, the custodians designated by both parties shall jointly open the boxes, divide the items into groups, and inventory and receive them according to the list. Both parties shall sign and seal the list. After each box is inventoried, it shall be immediately repacked, jointly sealed, and supervised for transportation into the warehouse. (3) The safekeeping procedures for the warehouse are as follows: 1. The custodians are as follows: (1) Two custodians designated by the Museum. (2) Two custodians designated by the Exhibition Office. (3) Staff members of the Custody Division of Section Two of the exhibition. 2. There are four keys to the warehouse, one held by the Museum, one by the Exhibition Office, and two by the staff members of the Custody Division of the exhibition. (3) The opening of the warehouse is scheduled for a specific time, and the custodians from each party shall jointly open and close the warehouse. (4) The procedures for retrieving exhibition items for examination are as follows: 1. During examination, at least one custodian from each party must be present to assist in the process. 2. During examination, the custodians from each party shall jointly supervise the removal of exhibition items for examination. After the examination is completed, the custodians shall continue to supervise the repacking of the items, jointly sealing them, and returning them to the warehouse. (4) The safekeeping measures during the preview exhibition are as follows: 1. When exhibition items are taken out of the warehouse, the custodians from each party shall jointly supervise the transportation of the original boxes to the exhibition venue, where they shall be unsealed and placed in display cabinets. The cabinets shall be locked, sealed, and registered in a list. In the case of calligraphy and paintings, the location where they are hung must also be noted. 2. The keys to the cabinets shall be jointly numbered, compiled, and stored in a safe deposit box. The safe deposit box shall be sealed and placed in the warehouse. When a key is needed, the custodians from each party shall jointly open the seal. After use, it shall be resealed and stored in the safe deposit box. 3. During the exhibition, in addition to the guards, the custodians from each party must continuously patrol the exhibition venue. 4. The opening and closing of the exhibition venue must be jointly supervised by the custodians from each party. The most valuable items and the most valuable calligraphy and paintings shall still be jointly supervised for storage and return to the warehouse after the exhibition closes each day. They shall be taken out and displayed again the next day according to the above-mentioned procedures. 5. Inside the exhibition venue, the custodians from each party must be on duty in shifts with the guards 24 hours a day. The shift arrangement shall be determined jointly by the custodians appointed by each party. The list of shift groups and the shift schedule shall be sent to each party for reference. (6) If a custodian from any party needs to take sick leave, he must entrust someone to act as his agent and must provide official written proof from the original dispatching organization. (7) When the preview exhibition is completed, all exhibition items shall still be jointly supervised for packing, sealing, and returning to the warehouse, and handed over to the Preparatory Committee. (8) If there are any matters not covered by these procedures, they shall be discussed and amended by the representatives of each party. (9) These procedures shall be implemented upon signature by the representatives of each party.

Overseas Chinese in Fiji No Longer Enjoy Consular Jurisdiction and Must Be Subject to Chinese Courts

According to the Greater Shanghai Evening News, the U.S. District Attorney in China, Watson, stated this morning (the 7th) that American courts will no longer handle cases concerning Philippine overseas Chinese as they used to. This is because the U.S. Congress recently passed a bill allowing the independence of Fiji, and Fijians are no longer U.S. citizens, but Fijian citizens. Now, if they go to the United States, they must also apply for passports from the U.S. consulates according to the methods for other foreigners. Therefore, they no longer enjoy consular jurisdiction in China and must be subject to Chinese courts.

Promoting Domestic Products in Southeast Asia; International Trade Bureau to Hold Meeting

According to the Central News Agency, the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industries has been working hard on investigating international markets and promoting domestic products. Recently, because the Ministry of Foreign Affairs sent Chen Chunpu to various parts of Southeast Asia to inspect various consulates, He Bingxian, the director of the International Trade Bureau, specially entrusted Chen to investigate the commercial situation abroad on its behalf. Yesterday, He spoke to the Central News Agency reporter about the recent trade situation and methods to save it, as follows:

Gathering Causes and Fundamentally Relieving

The decline of China's industry and commerce has led to the slump in international trade. The authorities are constantly preparing plans to save and develop it. Minister Chen previously went to Southeast Asia for inspection and returned to report that China's original market has been almost completely seized by others. He specially formulated principles and handed them over to the Bureau to find concrete ways to restore it. Now, Chen Chunpu is going to Southeast Asia for inspection again, and I have also entrusted him, out of personal friendship, to investigate the commercial situation in Southeast Asia, so as to gather causes extensively and seek fundamental relief.

Planning to Convene a Meeting to Save the Decline

The number of industrial and commercial products exported from China to Southeast Asia is very small, with only vegetables having a relatively large volume. Recently, overseas Chinese businessmen are very eager for Chinese to invest and compete there, but to save this situation, we must pool our wisdom and efforts. Therefore, the Bureau is now planning to convene the industrial and commercial sectors to jointly discuss methods to save it and seek self-improvement. All plans are in preparation and are expected to be realized in the short term.

Inflation Has No Impact

Looking at the countries around the world, although they are in an economic recession, their spirit of striving for development is admirable. China's recent trade imports and exports have decreased, but the rate of decrease in imports is greater than that in exports. The only reason for this is that the people's purchasing power is greatly reduced. Although the United States still ranks first in trade with China after implementing inflation, China's economic decline has not made special progress.

Foreign Affairs Commissioner Zheng Lin Departs the Country Yesterday

According to the Central News Agency, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs specially sent three commissioners, Chen, Zheng, and Liang, to Southeast Asia to inspect consulates and investigate overseas Chinese affairs and commercial conditions. Chen Chunguo has already left the country on the 5th. Eurasia Company Holds Memorial Service for Kalenberg Yesterday; Remains Cremated and Transported Back to Germany

Eurasia Airlines' Plane No. 3 on the Guangzhou-Beijing route crashed in Yizhang, Hunan, on the border of Hunan and Guangdong last month. The German pilot Kalenberg was injured and transported to Wuhan. Medical treatment was ineffective, and he passed away. His remains were transported to Shanghai by his wife by ship some days ago and placed in a coffin at the International Funeral Parlor. In memory of Mr. Kalenberg, Eurasia Company held a memorial service at the International Funeral Parlor on Jiaozhou Road at 3:00 PM yesterday. In addition to Huang Jiangquan, the chairman of the company, Li Jingcong, the general manager, and all the staff, those who attended the memorial service included German Consul General in Shanghai Klieber, Walde, the representative of Hanza Company, Stetz, the representative of Yong Chongsi Aircraft Factory, and representatives of German residents in Shanghai, about 100 people in total. Li Jingcong presided over the service, and the representatives delivered eulogies. The service ended around 4:00 PM. Mr. Kalenberg's remains are scheduled to be cremated at the funeral parlor today, and his wife will take his ashes back to Germany for burial within days.

Japanese Naval Landing Forces Held Combat Exercises Yesterday; 2,500 Japanese Soldiers Participated; Residents Were Not Disturbed Due to the Late Hour

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, the Japanese naval landing forces stationed in Shanghai held combat exercises in the Yangshupu area from 12:00 AM the night before last until 7:00 AM yesterday morning. The exercises were commanded by Commander Araki of the landing forces, and 2,500 Japanese soldiers participated. They first gathered near the Gongda Cotton Mill in Yangshupu, Shanghai East, and the exercise area included the Hongkou, Jing'an Temple Road, and Yangshupu Suzhou Creek areas, which were conducted in a three-pronged offensive style, with the central area of Hongkou as the target. During the exercises, machine gun teams, tank teams, etc. were all dispatched to boost morale. The exercises ended at 7:00 AM yesterday morning, and all the Japanese soldiers gathered at the Japanese barracks on North Sichuan Road and returned to their teams. The Japanese side notified the Chinese public security authorities of the truth during the exercises, and the exercises were conducted late at night, so the residents were not particularly disturbed.

Li Tianzhen's Proposal for Spring Disaster Relief in Jiangsu Province

Li Tianzhen, Deputy Director of the Jiangsu Province Disaster Relief, recently conducted on-site disaster relief in Changzhou, Zhenjiang and Nanjing counties, learning about the tragic situation of the people in the disaster areas and the urgent need for relief. Yesterday, it was heard that he had a proposal, which was sent to the Early Disaster Relief Association of the provinces. The original text is recorded below. Respectfully, I, Tianzhen, was entrusted by the conference to serve as the Deputy Director of Disaster Relief in Jiangsu Province. For more than half a year, I have been running around in the disaster areas and deeply feel that the drought suffered by various counties in Jiangsu Province last year was rare in the disaster relief in the past 20 years. The most serious ones are Liyang, Lishui, Jurong; followed by Gaochun, Jintan, Yixing, Yizheng, Liuhe; followed by Jiangpu, Zhenjiang, Wujin, Jiangdu. Although there are slight differences in comparison, the disaster situation is serious everywhere. The affected people have no food to cook, and they are lifeless. Ferns and bracken have been searched and exhausted, and it is difficult to even get enough bran and chaff to eat. They cry for hunger and cold, sell their sons and daughters, and some even flee their homes or commit suicide as a family. Among them, the number of people who died of starvation is unknown. All kinds of situations are heartbreaking to see, sad to hear, and too unbearable to describe, nor can they be fully described in writing. The suffering is that the disaster is widespread and the funds are limited. If the original number of urgent relief funds is used for inspection and release, it is really impossible to implement. As a last resort, I returned to Shanghai to make a final appeal to all parties. As a result, the counties received as much as 20,000 to 30,000 yuan, followed by only several thousand yuan. Like a cup of water to put out a cartload of burning firewood, it is still not enough. Fortunately, the Jiangsu Provincial Government has a plan to use work as disaster relief, raising huge funds to dredge rivers on a large scale. This can not only relieve the disaster temporarily, but also seek permanent benefits. It is a good idea in every way. However, only the strong men can get enough to eat, and the old, weak, women, and children cannot help but regret it. Moreover, it cannot be without worry. This work relief should be done during the winter farming season. I, Tianzhen, have been to various counties for inspection and release of urgent relief. Some of them have not yet started construction due to incomplete measurement, or because the entire project has not been approved by the provincial departments. However, now it is spring, and spring water will occur in a blink of an eye, which will obstruct dredging. The farming season is also approaching, and it is also impossible to recruit workers. Forcing to proceed will inevitably lead to abandonment halfway, wasting relief funds, and abandoning previous achievements. This is a great loss to the original intention of doing work relief. At this time of year, when the supply is not yet ready, work relief cannot be carried out, and spring relief cannot be planned, it is estimated that there are hundreds of thousands of disaster victims in each county. It is impossible to sit and wait for death, so the people's hearts are floating, which must be prevented. The disaster is so great that it is unimaginable. I, Tianzhen, dare not deliberately alarm the public, but I feel that the situation is dangerous and it is difficult to remain silent. Now, for the sake of prudent facts and weighing the advantages and disadvantages, I propose to ask the conference to approve and quickly send a telegram to the Jiangsu Provincial Government, ordering the counties that have started work on dredging rivers for work relief to complete the important projects as soon as possible within a limited time. Those that have not yet started work at all will stop working immediately. The remaining work relief funds will be distributed to the county magistrates according to the original number, ordering them to verify and distribute them to the disaster victims in each district as spring relief and for the need to purchase seeds. If this can be done, it will be of great benefit to local security. The matter is of great importance, so I dare to express my opinion. Whether it is feasible, I am extremely apprehensive and eagerly awaiting orders.

### Horrific Case of Chinese Woman Beaten to Death: Concession Authorities Promise to Investigate, Shanghai West Residents Held Meeting Yesterday to Respond, Reaching Out to Party and Government Agencies for Support

According to the Huadong News Agency, regarding the case of the British police officer, Stanford, from the Putuo Road Station, beating the vegetable-selling woman, Zhao Liujiali, to death on Yichang Road, the residents of Shanghai West have formed a support association for the victim. They have approached the municipal authorities and the police station to demand punishment for the perpetrator, as previously reported. Yesterday morning at 10 AM, the residents of Shanghai West held a general membership meeting at the fourth district branch of the residents' association. More than 500 merchants from Shanghai West attended. The atmosphere at the meeting was very tense. As a result, Chen Weiren, Wu Shuying, and Zhu Qizhen were appointed as representatives to visit Mr. Jullerat, the police chief of the Shanghai Municipal Council Police Department on Jiangxi Road, at 2 PM, to present the details of the incident and demand strict punishment and compensation for the offending Western police officer. Jullerat did not agree. They then went to Jiujiang Road to meet with Mr. Ansley, the deputy police chief of the Shanghai Municipal Council Police Department, to make the same request. Both police chiefs expressed their regret over the incident but stated that because they did not know the details, they would investigate and then handle the matter accordingly. If this incident occurred, they would deal with it severely according to the law. The three representatives were satisfied. They then went to the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, the Social Affairs Bureau, and other agencies to petition. All agencies agreed to provide support. The three representatives then left. At the same time, the fourth district branch of the Shanghai West residents' association sent a circular to residents of all districts, asking for assistance. The Shanghai Special District Residents' Federation sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council yesterday regarding the unwarranted beating to death of the vegetable-selling girl, Zhao Liujiali, from Yichang Road, by a Western police officer from the Public Concession. The original letter stated: "We are writing to inform you that according to a statement from resident Zhao Yongru, who lives at 76 Zhujiawan, Zhabei, his daughter, Zhao Liujiali, was selling vegetables at the Lid You Factory Alley on Yichang Road on the morning of March 5th at approximately 7 AM. Unexpectedly, while walking, she encountered a Western police officer No. 62 from the Putuo Road Station, who, without asking why, came forward to drive her away. At that time, the woman Zhao immediately walked away to avoid him, but the Western police officer forcefully pursued her and struck her head with his fist. She immediately fell to the ground injured and was helped up by her grandmother. The Western police officer not only refused to allow her to be helped up but also punched and kicked her grandmother. She was then sent to the Guangren Hospital on Avenue Haig via ambulance, but unfortunately, she died en route. Yongru is heartbroken but feels helpless because he is powerless and his voice is not heard. Therefore, he is submitting the facts to your Federation for assistance to redress the injustice and uphold national rights. It is our understanding that if street vendors do not violate police regulations, police officers should be responsible for protecting them. If there is a violation of police regulations, they should be detained at the police station for detailed questioning to determine whether they should be punished. However, this Western police officer did not follow this procedure and instead, without asking why, arbitrarily used force to beat an innocent person, resulting in death. He treats the law like discarded straw and human life like grass. Such unfortunate incidents are caused by your Bureau's Western police officers who are familiar with the law, indicating that police training has been neglected. The brutality and unreasonableness are not in line with the civilized world, and the security of the municipality in the future is a cause for concern. In order to protect the lives of citizens and the safety of the municipality, our Federation cannot remain silent. We hereby lodge a serious protest, demanding prompt punishment of the perpetrator, compensation, and an apology to our government authorities. Please do not disregard this and provide a reply." The Federation also sent letters to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Concession and the Chinese Directors to jointly lodge protests to facilitate the process.

### Suicide of Nursing Student at Red Cross Hospital No. 2: Fearing Layoffs, He Secretly Took Poison, Rescue Efforts Failed, Resulting in Death

Lu Xiyao, a nursing student at the Chinese Red Cross Hospital No. 2 on Xinzha Road, was from Suiyuan. He was 23 years old. He was one of the orphans recruited from the north and brought to Shanghai for care by the Association in the autumn of the 18th year of the Republic. Because of his quiet character and careful conduct, he was recruited as a nursing student by the hospital director, Wang Peiyuan. Recently, he was assigned to the pharmacy to learn formulation, and his work was making progress. His monthly salary was six yuan. He often lamented his tragic life and the fact that he could not afford clothes in addition to paying for night school tuition with his monthly salary. Recently, the Association received instructions from the Ministry of Interior to tighten expenses and reduce the budget from two thousand five or six hundred yuan to one thousand five hundred yuan. This would inevitably lead to layoffs and salary cuts. Therefore, the student, anticipating being laid off and facing a lonely and wandering life, secretly entered the pharmacy the night before (the 4th), stole poison, and went to his dormitory to commit suicide. When the hospital director checked on his work the next morning, he assumed that the student had not yet gotten up and ordered a servant to wake him in his room. Only then was it discovered that he had taken poison. Despite the hospital's best efforts to save him, it was too late, and he died at around 11 PM the night before.

### Another Eleven Depositors Accuse Jiande Bank: Only Chai Chuangui Surrenders, Firmly Requests Extension for Reconciliation with Plaintiffs

The collapse of Jiande Bank has now been almost three months, and there is still no resolution to the debts. The shareholders and general manager of the bank, including Chai Chuangui, have been repeatedly sued by creditors such as Wei Haijiang to the First Special District Court for fraud and embezzlement, and have been repeatedly summoned, as previously reported. It is now learned that eleven savings depositors of the bank, including Hu Qingxiang, Luo Hongji, Xu Bolun, Zhang Yiyuan, Tang Jinshu, Hu Xinpei, Zou Jiaquan, He Miaohong, Jiufeng Xinji, and Yong Taiyuan, have also jointly hired lawyers to file a lawsuit against the bank's directors and general manager for fraud and embezzlement. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui opened the court session. Unexpectedly, only Chai Chuangui surrendered among the defendants. The others, Chen Xifu, Chai Yousheng, Tu Kaizheng, Li Jingwei, Yan Ziyu, Yan Keming, Ma Suizhi, Ou Jiancheng, and Zheng Huairong, all avoided appearing in court. The accountant from the clearing house, Mr. Pan, submitted seven or eight related account books to the court as instructed. The plaintiff's lawyer then stated the intent of the lawsuit, stating that the bank's capital was claimed to be one million, and it was claimed that fifty thousand was collected when registered, but the actual amount was only slightly more than twenty thousand. Not long after opening, the bank widely advertised a six-week anniversary celebration, adding one percent interest to deposits during the anniversary period. When the business failed, the responsible directors not only failed to declare bankruptcy according to the company law, but also secretly repurchased the bank's shares as it was on the verge of collapse. For example, Liang Yaoting was originally a shareholder of the bank, and Liang's shares were repurchased at that time so that Liang could relieve himself of shareholder responsibility. All of these actions were fraudulent to depositors, embezzling deposits, and violating company regulations. The total amount of money defrauded from the plaintiffs in this case is more than three thousand yuan. Therefore, in addition to requesting that the defendants be punished according to law, they also requested that they be ordered to repay the principal and interest. When questioned, the defendant Chai Chuangui insisted on requesting an extension, saying that the authorities and the plaintiffs were reconciled. The plaintiff's lawyer immediately said that the defendant's request for an extension based on the possibility of reconciliation was purely a delaying tactic, and that the defendant was now doing his best to buy up the bank's savings passbooks, because he had seen through the weakness of the average depositor, knowing that they were not wealthy, and was taking the opportunity to buy back the passbooks with six percent cash, forcing the depositors to sacrifice. Judge Liu then said that many of the plaintiffs had also not arrived, so the session was adjourned for further questioning.

### Midnight Show: Teenage Girl's Fatal Misstep, Cao Ding Complains Against Xia Jinrong

Cao Ding, a Suzhou woman residing at 122 Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession, is 47 years old. Her husband was a well-known rascal, nicknamed "Lame Foot Agen," and has since passed away. She has a daughter named Qiaoyun, who is 16 years old. She is pretty. She entered Yangxing Primary School when she was 11 or 12 years old and studied there for three years. Recently, she dropped out of school and stayed at home, unmarried and waiting to be betrothed. Xia Jinrong, the son of Xia Laosan (who was from Hubei and is now deceased), the owner of the Yuquanchi Bathhouse at No. 4 Jixiang Street, is 27 years old. He owns hundreds of thousands of dollars in inheritance and likes to be frivolous and wandering, frequenting entertainment venues and engaging in affairs. On the evening of January 23rd (the 19th day of the twelfth lunar month), Xia and two friends, Wang and Sun, went to Cao's house. At that time, Qiaoyun's younger sister, Su Lili, was also present. Xia and the other two invited Cao Ding, her daughter Qiaoyun, and Su to go to the Tianchan Stage on Fourth Avenue to see a play. When the show ended at midnight, everyone left their seats and went out the door. The theater entrance was crowded with people. Xia followed Qiaoyun and Lili, and Xia Ding, Wang, and Sun were separated from them. Xia then used his seductive skills and invited Qiaoyun and Lili to have some snacks, luring them to room 504 on the fifth floor of the Oriental Hotel on Tibet Road. After eating snacks, Lili took a bath and returned home alone. Qiaoyun was forced to stay overnight by Xia and was forcibly raped that night. The next day, they got up and separated. When Qiaoyun returned home, her mother asked where she had stayed the night before. Qiaoyun concealed the truth from her mother, falsely claiming that she had stayed at Su Lili's house. Ding did not think much of it. It was not until the Lantern Festival that Ding discovered that Qiaoyun had been raped by Xia, and she was shocked. She negotiated with Xia, but Xia not only refused to admit it but also used abusive language. Ding was extremely resentful and could not bear it any longer. Therefore, in her capacity as legal guardian, she hired a lawyer with her daughter to file a lawsuit in the criminal court of the Special Third Court, accusing Xia Jinrong of violating Article 240, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Law for raping a girl under the age of fifteen, endangering public morals, and Article 257 of the same law for abducting a minor, separating her from the person with parental rights, arbitrarily raping her, and endangering the family. At the same time, she collected evidence to prepare for the case. The court issued a summons based on the lawsuit and sent police officers to serve the parties, scheduling a hearing for the afternoon of the next day, presided over by Judge Li Changnian.

### Ruan Lingyu Case to be Heard Tomorrow: Yesterday, Some People Already Tried to Reserve Seats at the Courthouse, Court Officials Respond that Courthouse is Not a Theater

Ruan Lingyu, a Cantonese actress and leading actress in a certain film company, whose childhood name is A Gen and who is 26 years old, met Zhang Damin, a wealthy son (currently at 650 North Sichuan Road) while walking in the Kunshan Garden in Hongkou when she was seven years old. Their love developed into cohabitation. The following year, Zhang's mother passed away in Guangdong. Zhang and Ruan returned to their hometown to attend the funeral. Ruan first observed filial piety in the position of a daughter-in-law, and after a hundred days, the two were hastily married in the mourning hall. Afterwards, they came to Shanghai together and formed a small family in Hongkou. Because Zhang worked as a comprador for the Ruian Shipping Company in Taikoo Company in Hong Kong, he served on the ships and feared that Ruan would feel lonely living alone in Shanghai, so he adopted a daughter, named Miaorong (that is, Xiaoyu), to accompany her. In the 20th year, they moved to Dasheng Hutong on Haig Road in the French Concession. Ruan, through the introduction of Zhang's brother, Zhang Huichong, became an actress at the Star Film Company, while Zhang continued to do business in Hong Kong. At this time, Ruan developed a love affair with Tang Xiushan, a wealthy businessman from the same hometown in Hong Kong. She rented another house at 21, Lane 147, Haig Road to live in. In the spring of the 22nd year, Zhang went to Beijing from Hong Kong on business and visited home on the way. He saw that Ruan was living with Tang and left in a fit of anger. The next day, Ruan appointed lawyer Wu Chengyu to make an agreement for Zhang to sign to end their relationship. Zhang requested that Ruan return the clothes, furniture, and other items she had purchased. Ruan agreed to return them, but at that time, Zhang was unable to stay in Shanghai and hurriedly went to Hong Kong to become the director of the Business Tax Bureau in Fujian Province. Until the Fujian Incident occurred some years ago, Zhang returned to Shanghai. In the winter of last year, he hired a lawyer to send a letter to Ruan Lingyu asking her to fulfill the previous conditions and return the clothes and other items. Recently, Ruan broke her promise, and Tang instead filed a lawsuit in the First Special Court against Zhang Damin for defamation. As a result, he was found not guilty. Recently, Zhang Damin hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the primary criminal court of the Second Special Court, accusing Ruan Lingyu of forgery, embezzlement, theft, and other crimes. He also sued Ruan Lingyu and Tang Xiushan in the local criminal court for abduction and adultery. The court, based on the lawsuit, issued a summons on the 27th of last month, by Judge Sun Penghian of the primary court, to both parties for a hearing. The defendant Ruan Lingyu claimed to be ill and did not attend. The court reviewed the case file and determined that the case was related to the case in the local court, and ruled to wait for the transfer to the local court for a joint hearing. It has been reported before. It is now learned that the local criminal court of the Second Special Court has issued a summons, sent police to notify both parties and inform both lawyers, and scheduled a hearing for the afternoon of the 9th (that is, tomorrow). The occurrence of this case, after being reported in the newspapers, has attracted the attention of fans and people from all walks of life in Shanghai. It is expected that the court will be crowded with spectators tomorrow. What is even stranger is that yesterday morning, someone went to the registration office of the Second Special Court to request to reserve seats, fearing that it would be crowded at the time and that they would not be able to enter the court to see the splendor of both parties. The clerk at the registration office replied that the court was a solemn place, not a theater where tickets could be reserved, and rejected the request. The person left disappointed. It is heard that the judicial police chief of the Second Special Court, because the hearing of this case will be crowded with spectators and disrupt the order of the court, will send French police officers to supervise the court police to maintain order and check admission tickets. Those without tickets will be denied entry to the court.

### Shanghai Municipal Council to Purchase Land at the Corner of Nanjing Road and Henan Road: Real Estate Committee Ruling Results in Price of Over 330,000 Yuan

In order to widen the road, the Shanghai Municipal Council plans to purchase the land at the southeast corner of Nanjing Road and Henan Road, totaling one mu, two fen, and ling eight hao. Mrs. Hardoon, the owner, demanded over 564,108 yuan. This matter was submitted to the Real Estate Committee for arbitration. The Real Estate Committee met on January 31st, and representatives from both parties attended the debate (detailed information can be found in the Municipal Council Gazette). After deliberation by the committee, it was ruled that the land, which is one mu, two fen, and ling eight hao, should be valued at 410,720 yuan, minus the increased value of the remaining land of 73,000 yuan, so the actual price should be 337,720 yuan. The landlord has now notified the tenants to vacate the premises on schedule. The road widening work at that location will begin soon.

### French Concession Prohibits the Sale of Pufferfish

Punishment for Trafficking in Persons

Last month, at approximately 7:00 PM on the 20th, Chinese detectives Wang Runhe and Zhang Faxiang of the Hongkou Police Station uncovered a human trafficking operation at 105 North Jiangxi Road. They arrested three suspects: Jiang Yongqing from Tongzhou, Qiao Wengui from Jiangbei, and Ma A'mei, a Cantonese woman. The investigation revealed that from December of last year to February of this year, they had lured and abducted Min Fenghuang, 14 years old, from Liyang; Zhang Fuying, 11 years old; and Jin Di, 6 years old, from Wuxi, and sold them, dividing the proceeds for their own use. They were handed over to the First Special District Court for interrogation and sentencing. Yesterday morning, Wu Zehan, the judge, came to the Third Criminal Court and sentenced Yongqing to two years and six months imprisonment, Qiao Wengui to six months imprisonment, and Ma A'mei to eight months imprisonment, with a fine of 80 yuan. The number of days of pre-trial detention will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days.

Liu Xiangsun, Former Shanghai Daotai, Sued by His Nephew's Widow; Unable to Endure Oppression After Her Husband's Death, She Took Her Son and Left; Uncle Says Household Affairs are in His Brother's Hands and He Can't Help; Zhou Heying Files Criminal Complaint for Abandonment

Liu Xiangsun, from Hangzhou, who served as the Shanghai Daotai in the late Qing Dynasty, is now elderly and has been a resident of Shanghai since the Republic. He currently resides at No. 1 Gordon Road in Western Shanghai. Liu has four brothers, and he is the eldest. His second brother, named Zhongchang, also has four sons. The eldest, Zengbao, married a woman from Ningbo named Zhou Heying in the 11th year of the Republic (1922). Unexpectedly, Zengbao died suddenly the following year. Fortunately, Zhou gave birth to a son, continuing the family line. From then on, she remained chaste and raised her son with great hardship. She did not change her mind despite being a young widow. However, the Liu family in their ancestral home was a large, undivided household. After her husband's death, Zhou was frequently oppressed by the head of the family. At first, she endured it, but later found it impossible to live together. In the 14th year of the Republic (1925), she took her orphaned son from Hangzhou to Ningbo. As she had no parents or brothers, she temporarily stayed at her sister's home and obtained a teaching position at Zhongshan School in Ningbo, using her salary to make a living. She also tutored her son. However, the tuition fees were never enough to support their livelihood, so she repeatedly wrote to her father-in-law, Liu Zhongchang, asking for assistance. Zhongchang always excused himself by saying that household affairs were handled by Xiangsun, and he could not help. Zhou had no choice but to turn to her uncle-in-law, but each year she received only 40 gold yuan. Fortunately, her sister was very affectionate and lent her money whenever she was short, preventing her from freezing or starving. This year, she began teaching at the Xindan Elementary School on Yuezhou Road in this city, so she and her son moved to Shanghai. Her son, A'ming (also known as Zhonghe), is now twelve years old and is also studying at Xindan. However, having lived in Ningbo for many years, she has accumulated debts of over 4,000 gold yuan to her sister. Her sister, Wu Zhou, unwilling to sacrifice such a large sum, recently filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Court. After summoning both parties and questioning them, the judge kindly advised them to resolve the case peacefully, as they were sisters. He ordered Zhou Heying to repay in installments. Afterwards, Zhou, considering her current situation precarious, had no spare capacity to repay the debt. She thought about the family property her late husband should have inherited. As the Liu family had not divided their assets for several generations, and now they were all controlled by Liu Xiangsun, the living expenses for her and her son should naturally be provided by Xiangsun. She could not allow this abandonment to continue. Therefore, she hired a lawyer to file a criminal self-accusation against her uncle-in-law, Liu Xiangsun, in the name of her son A'ming's legal representative, for abandonment. She also attached a civil suit requesting a monthly living allowance of 50 yuan and 5,000 yuan for A'ming's education expenses. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Jiang Shuzi of the First Special District Court summoned the defendant, but he claimed to be ill and did not appear. He also hired a lawyer to defend him. After Zhou Heying stated the facts of the lawsuit, the witness Liu Pingzong, Zhou's nephew, testified. He said that he is currently a professor at Jiaotong University, the defendant is his uncle, Zhongdang is his father, the plaintiff is his sister-in-law, and A'ming is his nephew. After his brother Zengbao died, his sister-in-law insisted on moving out, and they could not stop her. Later, they repeatedly urged her to return, but she refused. The family property has not yet been divided among his brothers. Now, his parents still hope his sister-in-law will return, as they miss their grandson very much and have not seen him for ten years. The court then adjourned for another hearing.

Yixing Compatriots Organize Yixing Disaster Relief Efforts

Last year, Yixing suffered a severe drought, second only to Linyang in severity. The total number of affected people was 120,000, and deaths from starvation were reported daily. Pan Xulun, Sha Wuceng, Zong Boxuan, Zhou Boying, Zhu Rongzhuang, and other executive and supervisory committee members of the Yixing Association in Shanghai felt it was their inescapable duty to provide disaster relief to their hometown. Therefore, last autumn, they organized the Yixing Drought Relief Shanghai Branch under the Yixing Association in Shanghai, uniting with compatriots in Beijing, Hubei, and Tianjin to jointly raise relief funds. They also appealed to various charitable organizations in this city, such as the Provincial Drought Relief Association, the Red Swastika Society, the Sino-Foreign Relief Association, and the Jisheng Association, for assistance. These organizations generously donated funds to organize winter relief. The Red Swastika Society allocated 10,000 yuan, the Sino-Foreign Relief Association allocated 5,000 yuan, the Provincial Drought Relief Association allocated 3,000 yuan, the Yixing Drought Relief Association headquarters raised 10,000 yuan, and the Shanghai Branch raised 5,000 yuan, totaling 33,000 yuan, which was used to purchase flour and distribute it to provide emergency relief. Now that the winter relief has ended, the 120,000 victims are still crying out for food, and they lack seeds for summer planting. If spring relief is not continued, they will be left to die. It is now known that Pan Xulun, the chairman of the Yixing Association in Shanghai, has repeatedly pleaded with the Sino-Foreign Relief Association and the Jisheng Association, requesting them to send personnel to Yixing to distribute spring relief on their behalf. These associations have agreed to undertake this, but the relief funds must be at least 50,000 yuan, and Yixing compatriots must provide half of the funds. Mr. Pan consulted with these associations and the Yixing Drought Relief Association, and it has been agreed that the Jisheng Association, the Sino-Foreign Relief Association, the Yixing Drought Relief Committee, the Headquarters, and the Shanghai Branch will each donate 12,500 yuan, totaling 50,000 yuan, which will be handed over to the Jisheng Association to send personnel to Yixing to distribute. Recently, Pan Xulun has handed over the 12,500 yuan raised by Yixing compatriots living abroad to the Sino-Foreign Relief Association (including more than 6,600 yuan donated and raised by Mr. Pan himself, 800 yuan raised by Zhu Rongzhuang through calligraphy and painting, 1,000 yuan from compatriots in Beijing, more than 2,700 yuan from Jia Guobo and other compatriots in Hubei, 600 yuan from Ren Zhencai and other compatriots in Tianjin, and the remaining 900 yuan from the Yixing Shanghai winter relief donations.) The Yixing Drought Relief Association Headquarters has also remitted 6,000 yuan to the Jisheng Association in advance.

Follow-up on the Zhabei Robbery Case; Suspects Claim They Were Not Robbers; All Six Handed Over to Separate Sections

The Zhabei Xinza Police Station's Tanziwan Police Outpost escorted two suspects in a theft case, Wu Kaijue and Sun Jinhong, at 3:10 PM the day before yesterday. They were robbed by Wu San and others at the railway crossing. Wu San, Bao Genpei, Li Xiaofuzi, and Ling Yangsheng, the alleged robbers, were apprehended at the time, and along with the plaintiff Jiang Zongtang and three others, were sent to the Xinza Police Station. While they were being interrogated, Wu Er handed over his younger brother Wu Kaijue and others, and Wu Kaijue and Sun Jinhong suddenly surrendered themselves. These events were reported in yesterday's newspaper. Now it is known that the plaintiff stated that after the theft that night, he immediately reported it to the Tanziwan Police Station, which dispatched police to arrest Wu Kaijue and Sun Jinhong. Unexpectedly, while being escorted to the station, Wu San and others robbed Wu Kaijue and Sun Jinhong at the railway crossing. Fortunately, I reported it to the Tanziwan Police Station by phone, which dispatched a large number of police officers to arrest Wu San and the other four. However, no evidence was found at the time, so Wu San and others turned on me, saying they wanted me to "pull the table" (a slang term for gangsters, meaning to treat them to several tables of wine). Wu San stated that he initially did not intend to rob Wu Kaijue and others, but was trying to plead with the police officer, Lu Wenxing. Unexpectedly, the police officer did not recognize him, which led to a scuffle. Wu Kaijue and Sun Jinhong both stated that when they were being escorted to the station, they saw them fighting, so they took the opportunity to escape. They did not intend to do so. Later, realizing that things were not going well, they surrendered themselves. Bao Genpei and Li Xiaofuzi admitted to being friends with Wu San, but denied helping to rob Wu Kaijue and Sun Jinhong. Ling Yangsheng insisted that he did not know Wu San and the others, and had been mistakenly arrested. After reviewing the statements, interrogator Zheng Zuhan determined that the case involved robbery and fell within the scope of criminal law, which this branch station was not authorized to handle. Therefore, he ordered that the plaintiff Jiang Zongtang, the defendants Wu San, Wu Kaijue, Sun Jinhong, Bao Genpei, Li Xiaofuzi, and Ling Yangsheng, all six of them, be handed over to the third section of the Public Security Bureau's Zhabei branch yesterday afternoon at approximately 5:00 PM for further action.

Publishing World

*Hanxue Monthly*, Volume 4, Issue 6: The Hanxue Monthly, Volume 4, Issue 6, published by the Hanxue Bookstore, is "A Special Issue on Jiangxi Province." It has already been published. The content offers detailed descriptions, methods, and narratives of various responsible figures. It also includes an article written by Madam Soong Mei-ling entitled "Anecdotes of Bandit Suppression," which is of particular importance to the historical materials of the Republic's restoration. It is truly a valuable reference for those studying practical politics.

*Chinese Painting Monthly*, Special Issue on Chinese and Western Landscape Painting Thought: The *Chinese Painting Monthly*, a special issue on Chinese and Western landscape painting thought, edited by He Tianjian and Xie Haiyan and published by the Chinese Painting Association, has been published today. The content includes historical investigations, demonstrations of techniques, and analysis and comparison of ideas. The contributors, such as Zheng Wuchang, Huang Baohong, Sun Fuxi, Chen Baoyi, Yu Jianhua, Ni Yi, and Li Baoquan, are all prominent figures in the modern art world. The issue includes over thirty illustrations of famous Chinese and Western works by artists such as Wu Daozi, Huang Zijiu, and Da Vinci. It is printed on cream-colored Shulin paper in a regular script movable type edition. This issue is twice as long as usual and retails for 30 cents per copy. The content is very exciting. Furthermore, the fifth issue is the second part of the Special Issue on Chinese and Western Landscape Painting Thought. To encourage readers' interest, a large color print of Song Dynasty Li Di's landscape painting masterpiece is added. This painting is one of the most famous objects in the world of art and retails for 20 cents. Annual subscribers are not charged extra. It will be published on the 15th of this month.

*"A Tourist Guide to Wusong and Gaoqiao":* The Eighth District Educational Association of this city, in order to promote social education and provide guidance for people visiting the Eighth District, has commissioned Xu Zhengji and Su Shude to co-edit the book "A Tourist Guide to Wusong and Gaoqiao." It is a thick, pocket-sized volume in Western binding, containing photographs and various records on several hundred pages. It will be published soon. The Association predicts that the book will be highly sought after and plans to follow the precedent of last year's "A Survey of Education in the Eighth District," charging a small fee of five dimes per copy to limit distribution. Those who request copies by mail should include an additional two cents for postage. Requests can be sent to the Eighth District Educational Association at Wusong Middle School. The book is particularly suitable for elementary schools in Shanghai that wish to organize excursions to Wusong or Gaoqiao as part of their outdoor education curriculum. Wholesale discounts are available and interested parties can contact the Association directly.

*Journal of Geography*, Issue 4: The *Journal of Geography*, edited by the Geographical Society of China, has already published three issues, each with 500,000 words. It is known domestically for its rich materials and is an important publication in China's geographic field. It is reported that the fourth issue of the journal has been published this month. The content includes Ge Suicheng's "Research on Landscapes," "China's Borderlands in the Last Ten Years," Sheng Xugong's "The Spatial and Temporal Nature of Chinese Culture," Li Changchuan's "Research on Chinese Lakes," Chu Shaotang's "A Brief History of Chinese Maps," "The Great Flood of the Yellow River in 1933 and Its Control," and Lou Yunlin's "Japan's Trade Relations with China." In addition, there are nine local chronicles of this country, all new and detailed studies. Comrades who study geography should all have a copy. The price is 50 cents and it is distributed by the Dadong Bookstore in this city. It is also reported that in order to promote geography in China, the Society will change the journal from a quarterly to a monthly starting from Volume 2, Issue 1.

Film

First-Class Animal Film to be Shown in Paris: Animal films have been popular in recent years. Since the birth of *Tarzan the Ape Man*, the appeal of animal films has grown even stronger. The American Ediel Film Company has also recently produced an animal film entitled *Crawling Death*. The content is interspersed and has a unique flavor. It was filmed in the wilderness of the lower reaches of the Mexican Levalente Grande, so it is very different from animal films that use scenery. The fights between wild animals were filmed with a telescope, and the scenes are completely real, making people shudder when they see them. The whole film has many tense moments. In the scene where a tiger eats a monkey, after the tiger pounces on a lion, the monkeys cry sadly. A shepherd hears this and lets his water buffalo fight the tiger. The tiger is injured and a bear comes to eat it. The monkeys are overjoyed and dance around the buffalo to show their gratitude. The key point of the plot is that a couple separates due to disagreements. The wife takes her young son to the Grande. The young son spends his days with the natives and wild animals. When he grows up, he becomes extremely brave and falls in love with a native girl. Later, his father finds him and the family is reunited. The young son is the little Tarzan, played by young star Maurice Murphy. It is reported that this film will be shown at the Paris Grand Theater on Avenue Joffre, starting this Sunday.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:20 PM yesterday said that the barometric pressure in North China and the Yellow River basin continues to fall, indicating a low pressure system. It is expected to bring cloudy skies, cyclones, and sandstorms to the surrounding areas of Shandong tomorrow. There may be strong winds from the south to southwest along the coast. The weather in the Yangtze River basin is sunny and calm, with cloudy skies and smog in some areas. There is a light seasonal wind near the Ryukyu Islands. The skies around Taiwan are cloudy, with scattered rain and fog. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 70.0 degrees and the lowest was 43.0 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 63.7 degrees and the lowest was 33.6 degrees.
