Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

A Brief History of Film Development (11)

— Wen Ying

(11) The Completion of Techniques in the Silent Era

In (The Big Parade), directed by King Vidor, there is a scene where the male and female leads chew gum. The humor of that scene is something that anyone who has seen it will not forget. But how was it filmed? It's quite laughable to say. According to the original script, there was no scene of chewing gum. The male and female leads were just supposed to meet very simply. The male lead at that time was John Gilbert, and the female lead was French star Renee Adoree (her early death was also a great loss to the film industry).

Renee was on the set, waiting to start filming, when she was chewing gum in a relaxed manner. She accidentally said a sentence, saying that the country people in France had not seen this thing before the European War. After the end of the European War, when American soldiers went to France, this thing also became popular in France. King Vidor heard these words and shouted, "Great. John, give Renee a piece of gum to eat. Teach her how to eat it. She doesn't understand your language. You don't understand his language either. You use gestures to perform."

They had not even rehearsed it. Renee and John were neither prepared nor did they know what to do after eating the gum. The camera slowly shook. The photographer looked at the director's face, quietly waiting for him to shout "Cut". The director was looking at the male lead eating gum, and not shouting "Cut", which made the photographer wonder, eating some gum also required so much film, I don't know that King Vidor had different eyes, and what he saw was different from others. By the time that scene was filmed, it had become the longest single scene in all films ever. This can also be said to be a major reform in photography and directing techniques.

When the film was finished editing, the scene of eating gum was able to maintain its original perfection. After it was released to the public, the audience, after seeing the entire film, was most moved by that scene. The production cost of this small "program production" was less than $200,000, but after it was released, the box office revenue in New York alone exceeded $800,000. The success of this war film is conceivable, and the audience, after being tired of war, was able to uniquely welcome (The Big Parade), which also shows the fickleness of psychology, and the skill of a good director in manipulating people's hearts.

We don't need to lament the past glory. But the progress of Hollywood is extremely fast. Hollywood is a vivid, lively, young, and lovely thing, but all its vitality comes from the money that is produced from the blood of youth and abundance. Money, money, money is the blood of Hollywood, the source of life. Among the films with the largest investment in the silent era mentioned earlier, "Ben-Hur" was the first. In addition to money, the effort put into it by the people involved was also considerable. But that film is still an indelible masterpiece in history. The other few, such as "Beau Geste", "The Covered Wagon", "Phantom of The Opera", "Robin Hood", etc., must still be reverberating in your minds.

The advancement of film is extremely rapid, but the road it has traveled is not a smooth road. How many times has it almost been destroyed, but it has been able to turn danger into safety and turn misfortune into good fortune. Now everyone is making a "clean-up movement", which makes the film industry feel extremely uneasy, but the first patent war almost killed it. At the same time, it suffered a blow from "censorship", which almost made it slump. The film industry figures at that time were not without places where their actions were out of line, but they were able to rein in their horses at the edge of the cliff and turn back in time. They promised to abide by the rules in the future, and elected Will Hayes as Hollywood's moral inspector, which allowed them to safely overcome the difficulties and reach their current position.

When you look back, don't laugh at the simplicity and boredom of those silent films, because the best of them have already reached perfection in terms of technique. In the past thirty years, the development from "moving peep shows" to the technically perfect film industry is an amazing progress. Money has also become abundant, and it can hire great directors, first-class writers, and famous actors. It has reached a point where nothing is impossible. It has reached the peak of art. But, after a person reaches the highest peak, where else can he go? Just like thirty years ago, the audience was bored with simple moving films and had to add the editing of character stories, they now feel the same boredom. Film companies are gradually losing money. The audience in movie theaters is gradually thinning out. Could it be that after the completion of film techniques, it has reached the end of the road? (To be continued)

(Note: This article is not finished, but because the continuation has not arrived, it must be temporarily suspended. The following article turns to the sound film era).

Film Review

Review of "Resurrection"

— Ling He, You Jing

We Life Again—Nanjing Screening

1. Leo Tolstoy

Regarding Leo Tolstoy (1828–1910), the great Russian, and indeed global, artist, we cannot possibly write a sufficient biography within these brief pages. To gain a deeper understanding of the literary masterpiece "Resurrection," Tolstoy's artistic and religious views—representing the most vivid expression of so-called "Tolstoyan" thought—we will briefly examine his artistic theories and religious views within the context of his life.

Leo Tolstoy, like his contemporary, the other great writer Ivan Turgenev, was born into nobility and, through contact with real life, developed a deep dissatisfaction with his own class. After graduating from Kazan University, Tolstoy stayed with his older brother, a staff officer, in the Caucasus and soon took up a similar position himself. In contact with many soldiers, he became heavily influenced by the habits of young officers at the time and unwittingly fell into a life of drinking, gambling, and pleasure-seeking. This period of decline, one might say, later provided him with profound material for repentance in a completely different attitude toward life. In 1855, he participated in the Crimean War, witnessed all the horrors of the battlefield, and came to understand the nature of war at that time. This became the foundation for his later anti-militarism and thoroughgoing advocacy of pacifism. After the war, he roamed through England, France, and Germany, and combined with his observations after returning home, he had a deep and painful understanding of the darkness and ugliness of the so-called civilized world. A few years after his marriage, he cooled towards his already fruitful writing career and, as an enthusiast and practitioner of religious and social reform activities, threw a huge bomb at the civilization of the time. However, because of the dualism of the metaphysics from which he departed, and the return to and development of original Christian education, this bomb of his was not as powerful as he had thought.

You are poor, precisely because you are rich,

You are strong-willed, precisely because you are weak,

Mother Russia!

Tolstoy sang thus. On the one hand, Tolstoy was not only a genius artist who provided the world literary scene with excellent depictions of the real life of the Russian people, but also a fanatical Christian landowner. On the other hand, he was a relentless, strong, direct, and sincere opponent of social hypocrisy and deceit, yet as a Tolstoyan religious follower, he told the masses that although he himself was ugly, he was an intellectual engaged in the moral self-completion, a debilitated and mentally ill weakling. He mercilessly criticized the exploitative systems of the time, the autocracy of the Tsarist government, and even more deeply dissected the contradictions of society, but at the same time fanatically preached "non-resistance to evil" through violence. His contradictions in views and doctrines were not accidental but were a manifestation of the contradictory conditions in Russian life during the 1830s. Therefore, it is not enough to observe and evaluate Tolstoy's views solely from the perspective of the modern labor movement and scientific socialism; one should evaluate them from the perspective of the emerging capitalism, the impoverishment of the masses, and the loss of land, which inevitably gave rise to resistance from the autocratic countryside. Tolstoy was a great expression of the thoughts and spirits of millions of peasants at the time of the coming Russian bourgeois revolution.

2. "Resurrection"

The novel "Resurrection" is artistically inferior to "War and Peace," "Anna Karenina," and other short stories in Tolstoy's oeuvre. However, it is a masterpiece of Tolstoy's later years, the most concrete and explicit crystallization of his artistic and religious views, and the most cosmopolitan of the author's novels.

In "Resurrection," Tolstoy wove together the problems he encountered, the nodes of society at that time, the focus of darkness, and especially the attention to the issue of "land and freedom," and provided a solution through his religious views, under the guise of a love story. Especially in the second half, he played himself as Dmitry, repenting from his fallen sin and converting to religious anarchism, personally solving the problems of the masses he saw. This was originally a very ridiculous thing. But in Tolstoy's sincere, passionate, and tragic artistry, he cleverly achieved the effect he intended. This is what we must emphatically point out among those who unconditionally worship everything Tolstoy did.

3. "Resurrection" on the Screen

I remember we once saw "Nana," produced by Sam Goldwyn and starring Anna Sten. At the same time, we will not forget that Émile Zola's "Nana" was transformed under Goldwyn's production. That is to say, the Nana of the novel did not appear on the screen as she originally was, but Goldwyn's Nana appeared completely through the colored lenses of a businessman. Therefore, the loss in value of "Nana" caused considerable dissatisfaction among the audience. Now, Tolstoy's "Resurrection" has been brought to the screen under Goldwyn's wishful thinking, and like "Nana," it has changed the original face of the original novel.

To illustrate this point, we can cite the following proofs.

"Resurrection" became Tolstoy's representative work, and a world-renowned masterpiece, precisely because the last part had the development of Tolstoyism. Therefore, the male protagonist ultimately sacrificed himself to complete the love of Katusha Maslova and Simonson. Prince Dmitry single-handedly engaged in social undertakings. The so-called mechanical translation of the original Christian meaning "Matthew 5:39", kneeling before the icon, attempting to find a solution to social problems in the Bible.

It is in this place that the most central development of Tolstoyism lies, and the keynote for evaluating "Resurrection." At the same time, sacrificing one's own love for the sake of love is also expressed as Tolstoy's view of love. However, under Goldwyn's production, this focus was completely ignored, and the male and female protagonists were combined in a Happy Ending, distorting the marriage of Katusha and political prisoner Simonson in the original work, and distorting the spirit of Dmitry seeking a solution to social problems. Of course, we cannot have too high an evaluation of Tolstoyism at the current stage, so progressive filmmakers can boldly correct this error, but the playwrights have completely accepted the original religious art proposition, only removing the essence of the original work in the end, and then changed the original name Resurrection to (We Life Again), which is actually a vulgar (We Love Again).

Here, it is fully explained that the playwrights, under Goldwyn's instructions, did not have a good understanding of the original work, and further demonstrated technical flaws in other scenes. Most importantly, we must point out that when Katusha went to the train station to find Dmitry, in the silent film "Resurrection" (starring Dolores del Río), that was the most emotional scene, which made the audience cry bitterly. But in this film, it is so ordinary, not only does it rain for no reason as in the flower shed, but mainly it fails to create the climax effect of the tragedy. At the same time, before losing herself in the flower shed, Dmitry said that he would take her for a walk on a beautiful summer night, so the rain came too suddenly. What also needs to be pointed out is that because the time passed was explained by the subtitle "Seven Years Later", the process of the heroine becoming a prostitute and accidentally killing someone was not a pictorial expression but a dialogue explanation, so the audience did not have a clear understanding of the change in the personality of the character Katusha, but this was also the success of the silent film.

However, this film exaggerated the religious scenes as much as possible, as a positive reception to the original religious art sermon. At the same time, these places were quite successful technically due to Rouben Mamoulian's skilled directing techniques and the excellent performances of Fredric March and Anna Sten.

What should be mentioned in particular is that Mamoulian, after "Applause" and "Queen Christina," demonstrated his directing skills here. Within the scope stipulated by the script, he succeeded as an excellent technician no matter what. Naturally, we cannot fail to point out that the train station and other scenes showed errors in weaving techniques, thus losing the tragic emotion. However, his guidance on acting, or the handling of individual scenes, was very skillful. In particular, the cruel depiction of prisoner life, its power to stimulate the audience, was extremely successful in terms of film art. It is worthy of being a great literary work.

4. Conclusion

The fact that "Resurrection" has been brought to the screen many times shows how film merchants are exploiting world-famous works. However, when they distort the original work, they fully demonstrate the vulgarity of the merchant's attitude. The highest effect of tragedy has not been achieved here, although we have been greatly satisfied in terms of individual skills. However, soft gentlemen often juxtapose artistic value and political value, so if they do not deny that Tolstoy is an artist, how would they explain the sermon in "Resurrection"?

Anna Sten and Fredric March, the two leading actors of "Resurrection," performed in the immortal masterpiece of the great Russian writer Tolstoy

Anti-Imperialist Film "Beauty's Heart"

"Beauty's Heart," which has been in production for more than a year, has finally been completed recently.

"Beauty's Heart" is Xu Xinfu's powerful work following "Salt Tide." Its story depicts the daughter of a famous scholar who falls in love with a Northeast volunteer soldier. Engaged in constant warfare. Love threads cannot hold back ambition, and finally the volunteer soldier dies in battle on the battlefield. Amidst the emotions of sorrow and hatred, many other national heroes still proceed very seriously.

At a time when "high-ranking women do not know the hatred of national subjugation and still sing the Backyard Flower across the river," this anti-imperialist film is undoubtedly of great significance. It is a stimulant for the declining national spirit and those who are drunk and dreaming of death, making the audience want to cry but have no tears, and want to laugh but have no voice.

In terms of directing techniques, it is more perfect than "Salt Tide." Of course, the significance is also more serious than "Salt Tide." Coupled with many magnificent sets and delicate and profound expressions, it will be unexpectedly successful.

Starring Hu Die, Wang Zhengxin, Gu Meijun, Lan Jun, Xu Xin, etc. (However)
